Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Captive Spouse: Immediate Annulment of Marriage
Ruling with hadith proof regarding captive spouses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one spouse is captured and explain how the hadith of Ibn Abbas serves as the dalil for immediate annulment.

Core Idea
Captivity immediately dissolves the marriage, proven by the Prophet's prohibition of intercourse without a waiting period.

War and captivity have profound effects on marital bonds. This lesson examines the specific case where one spouse falls into enemy hands. The Hanafi school derives a clear ruling from a hadith narrated by Ibn Abbas, establishing that separation occurs at the moment of capture, not later.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
The source states: 'If one of them is taken captive, separation occurs between them.' Recognize that this applies whether the husband or the wife is captured.
Separation means the marriage is annulled (batil), not merely suspended.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The text cites a hadith from Ibn Abbas: the Prophet forbade intercourse with a captive woman until she gives birth (if pregnant) or until she menstruates once (if not pregnant). This hadith is transmitted by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi.
This is a Sunnah ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but it is still authoritative in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the legal implication (wajh al-dalalah)
The prohibition of intercourse with a captive implies that her previous marriage is dissolved. If the marriage were still valid, intercourse would be permissible without waiting (analogous to a husband with his wife). The required waiting period (istibra) confirms that a new relationship may commence, meaning the old one is void.
This is the key link between the hadith and the ruling: the prohibition proves annulment.
4
Note the methodological difference
Some early scholars held that captivity does not automatically annul the marriage. The Hanafi school, however, relies on this hadith and the principle that captivity changes legal status (slavery), which is incompatible with marriage. The mufta bihi is immediate annulment.
The disagreement is legitimate ikhtilaf, but the Hanafi position is established through the clear hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان سبى احدهما وقعت البينونة بينهما. عن ابن عباس قال نهى رسول الله ان توطأ حامل حتى تضع او حائل حتى تحيض.
And if one of them is taken captive, separation occurs between them. From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah forbade that a pregnant woman be approached until she gives birth, or a non-pregnant woman until she menstruates.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This lesson covers the scenario where one spouse (either husband or wife) is taken captive from Dar al-Harb. The ruling is that separation (baynuna) occurs immediately upon captivity. The Hanafi evidence is a hadith from Ibn Abbas: the Prophet forbade having intercourse with a captive woman until she gives birth (if pregnant) or until she menstruates once (if not pregnant). This implies that the previous marriage is dissolved, as otherwise intercourse with her would be adultery. The hadith establishes that the marriage of a captive woman is annulled by captivity. The same applies if the husband is captured, as the wife then becomes a captive in the hands of the enemy, and the marriage is dissolved due to the impossibility of marital life.

Key Terms
سبي (saby): Captivity in war; being taken as a prisoner or slave.
استبراء رحم (istibrāʾ ar-raḥim): The period to ensure the womb is empty of pregnancy before intercourse with a captive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the hadith about captive women serve as proof that marriage is dissolved upon captivity?
A) Because the husband is dead.
B) Because it prohibits intercourse until a waiting period, indicating the marriage is void.
C) Because the Prophet explicitly said so.
D) Because the wife is now owned by another.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the capture of one spouse immediately dissolves the marriage, as evidenced by the Prophet's prohibition of intercourse with a captive without waiting.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Both Spouses Captured Together: Marriage Persists
Ruling that joint captivity preserves the marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when both spouses are captured together from Dar al-Harb and explain the principle of ikhtilāf dārayn.

Core Idea
Joint captivity preserves the marriage because there is no difference of territory.

In the previous lesson, you learned that if one spouse enters Dar al-Islam alone, the marriage dissolves. But what if both are taken captive together? This lesson presents the opposite case: when both spouses are captured together, their marriage remains intact. The key is whether the couple is separated by territorial status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognise that both spouses are captured from Dar al-Harb and remain together—neither reaches Dar al-Islam alone.
2
Apply the principle of ikhtilāf dārayn
Check if the spouses are in different territories. If one is in Dar al-Islam and the other in Dar al-Harb, dissolution occurs.
This lesson deals with the case where both are together, so no territorial difference.
3
Determine territorial status
Since both are in captivity together, they are both in Dar al-Harb (or both in transit), so they share the same territorial status.
4
Conclude the ruling
Because no territorial difference exists, the marriage continues; no separation (baynūnā) occurs.
The marriage remains valid and no renewal is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان سبيا لا تقع البينونة بينهما. [Arabic incomplete in OCR; based on Urdu: اگر دونوں ساتھ قید ہوئے تو بینونت واقع نہیں ہوگی۔]
And if both are captured together, no separation occurs between them.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This lesson presents the opposite case from the previous: if both spouses are captured together from Dar al-Harb, their marriage is not dissolved. The reason is that the difference of dar (being in different territories) does not occur; they remain together in the same situation (captivity). Since marital life can continue (albeit in captivity), there is no need for separation. The Hanafi ruling relies on the principle that separation due to captivity only occurs when one spouse is in Dar al-Islam and the other remains in Dar al-Harb. If both are taken together, they are both in the same status, so the marriage persists. The Urdu commentary explicitly states 'اگر دونوں ساتھ قید ہوئے تو بینونت واقع نہیں ہوگی' (if both are captured together, separation does not occur).

Key Terms
اختلاف دارين (ikhtilāf dārayn): Difference of territory (Dar al-Islam vs. Dar al-Harb) that can cause legal effects like dissolution of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when both spouses are taken captive together from Dar al-Harb?
A) Their marriage is automatically dissolved.
B) Their marriage remains valid.
C) Only the wife's marriage dissolves.
D) They must renew their marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
Joint captivity preserves the marriage because both spouses remain under the same territorial jurisdiction.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Separation When One Spouse Is Captured
Ruling with proof that captivity of one spouse ends the marriage due to ikhtilaf al-dar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage dissolution when one spouse is captured and explain the legal cause (ikhtilaf al-dar) with its proofs.

Core Idea
Captivity of one spouse severs the marriage immediately due to difference of abode (ikhtilaf al-dar).

This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri addresses a scenario where a married couple is separated by war: one spouse is captured and brought to Dar al-Islam while the other remains in Dar al-Harb. The Hanafi school rules that their marriage is automatically dissolved. The commentary provides Quranic, hadith, and athar evidence to support this ruling. In this lesson, we will unpack the legal reasoning and understand why ikhtilaf al-dar is a decisive cause for dissolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its cause
The passage states that if one spouse is captured (sabi), separation (baynuna) occurs. The cause is ikhtilaf al-dar (difference of abode).
The capture must result in one spouse being in Dar al-Islam and the other in Dar al-Harb.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse indicating that a believing man cannot marry a polytheist woman implies that difference in religion ends the marriage. By analogy, difference in dar also ends it.
The passage refers to the verse: 'And do not marry polytheist women until they believe...' (Quran 2:221).
3
Examine the athar from Ibn Abbas
If a Christian woman converts to Islam before her husband, she becomes forbidden. This shows that a change in status immediately dissolves the marriage; captivity is an even stronger case.
The athar is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
4
Examine the hadith on istibra'
The Prophet prohibited intercourse with a captive woman until istibra' (one menstrual period) or until she delivers if pregnant. This proves that her prior marriage is terminated, otherwise istibra' would not be necessary.
Hadith from al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۴۰ (۱۱۵) وان سبى احدهما وقعت البينونة بينهما
یہ اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے کہ دونوں کا نکاح ٹوٹ گیا ہو۔ اس آیت میں یہ بھی ہے کہ مشرکہ مومن کے لئے اور مومنہ عورت مشرک کے لئے حلال نہیں ہیں۔ یہ بھی دلیل ہے کہ دونوں کا نکاح ٹوٹ گیا (۲) اثر میں ہے عن ابن عباس اذا اسلمت النصرانية قبل زوجها بساعة حرمت عليه ، وقال داؤد عن ابراهيم الصائغ سئل عطاء عن امرأة من اهل العهد اسلمت ثم اسلم زوجها في العدة اهى امرأته ؟ قال لا الا ان تشاء هي بنكاح جديد وصداق ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اسلمت المشرکۃ او النصرانية تحت الذمی اوالحربی ص ۷۹۶ نمبر ۵۲۸۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نصرانی کی بیوی مسلمان ہو جائے تو فورا نکاح ٹوٹ جائے گا تو جب وہ دار الحرب سے دار الاسلام ہجرت کر کے آئے گی تو بدرجہ اولی نکاح ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اختلاف دارین سے نکاح ٹوٹ جائے گا۔
[۱۸۴۰] (۱۱۵) اگر دونوں میں سے ایک قید ہو کر آیا تو دونوں میں جدائیگی ہو جائے گی۔
میاں بیوی میں سے ایک قید ہو کر آیا تو اختلاف دار ہو گیا۔ ایک دارالحرب میں رہا اور ایک دارالاسلام میں آگیا۔ اب زوجیت کی مصلحت باقی نہیں رہی اس لئے اس کا نکاح ٹوٹ جائے گا تا کہ نیا نکاح کر کے اپنی زندگی گزار سکے (۲) اگر عورت قید ہو کر آئی تو وہ آقا کی باندی بن گئی اس لئے آقا کے لئے صحبت کرنا جائز ہو گیا۔ اور یہ اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے جب پہلا نکاح ٹوٹ جائے۔ اس لئے تنہا عورت کے قید ہوتے ہی نکاح ٹوٹ جائے گا (۳) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال نهـى رسـول الـلـه ان توطأ حامل حتى تضع او حائل حتى تحيض ( دارقطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ، ص۱۸۰ نمبر ۳۳۵۹۸ و للبیہقی ، باب استبراء من ملک الامته ج سابع ص ۷۳۸، نمبر ۱۵۵۸۷) اس حدیث میں قیدی عورتوں کے بارے میں فرمایا۔ پہلے شوہر کے حمل سے ہو تو وضع حمل کے بعد وطی کرے۔ اور غیر حاملہ ہو تو ایک حیض گزرنے کے بعد استبراء رحم کر کے صحبت کرے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قیدی عورت کا نکاح ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ جنگ اوطاس کی قیدی عورتوں کی تفصیل مسلم شریف ، باب جواز ولی المسبیۃ بعد الاستبراء وان كان لها زوج الفسخ نکاحه بالسمی ص ۴۷۰ نمبر ۱۴۵۶ میں ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قید ہونے سے نکاح ٹوٹ جائے گا۔
If one of the two is captured, separation occurs between them.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that if one spouse (husband or wife) is taken captive and brought to Dar al-Islam while the other remains in Dar al-Harb, the marriage is immediately dissolved. This is due to ikhtilaf al-dar (difference of abode). The commentary provides proofs: (1) Quranic verse that disbelieving women are not lawful for believers, implying separation of religion also severs marriage; (2) Athar from Ibn Abbas that if a Christian woman converts before her husband, she becomes haram immediately; (3) Hadith forbidding intercourse with a captive woman without istibra', showing that captivity ends the prior marriage. The key principle is that the marriage cannot continue when the spouses cannot live together due to the division of dar.

Key Terms
سبي (sabi): Captivity, being taken as a prisoner of war and brought to Dar al-Islam.
بينونة (baynuna): Complete separation, dissolution of marriage.
اختلاف دارين (ikhtilaf al-darayn): Difference of abode between Dar al-Islam and Dar al-Harb.
استبراء (istibra'): Waiting for one menstrual period to confirm the womb is empty, required before intercourse with a newly acquired female slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband is captured and brought to Dar al-Islam while his wife remains in Dar al-Harb, what happens to their marriage?
A) The marriage remains valid until a judge divorces them.
B) The marriage is automatically dissolved due to ikhtilaf al-dar.
C) The marriage is suspended until they reunite.
D) The wife must wait for iddah and then may remarry.

Key Takeaway
Ikhtilaf al-dar is a legal cause that immediately dissolves the marriage when one spouse is captured and crosses the boundary between Dar al-Harb and Dar al-Islam.

No Separation When Both Spouses Are Captured Together
Ruling that joint captivity preserves marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that marriage continues when both spouses are captured together and explain the supporting evidence from Surah al-Mumtahanah (60:10).

Core Idea
Joint captivity preserves marriage; separation only if abodes differ.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Islamic jurisprudence: if a husband and wife are captured together from Dar al-Harb and brought to Dar al-Islam, does their marriage dissolve? The Hanafi school holds that it does not, based on the principle that ikhtilaf al-dar (difference of abode) is the cause of separation, and joint captivity means they share the same abode. The ruling is derived from the Quranic verse on not returning believing women to disbelievers, implying continuity when both are together.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The act is both spouses being captured together and brought to Dar al-Islam. The Hanafi ruling is that their marriage remains valid (sahih).
This is a clear ruling from the matn.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The main proof is the Quranic verse (Surah al-Mumtahanah 60:10): 'ولا تمسكوا بعصم الكوافر' (And hold not to the marriage bonds of disbelieving women). The commentary also cites an athar from Ibn Abbas and a hadith about captives.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse commands not to retain marriage bonds with disbelieving women. When both spouses are now in Dar al-Islam (presumably Muslims or protected dhimmis), the prohibition does not apply, implying that the marriage bond remains. The principle of ikhtilaf al-dar is not triggered because both are in the same abode.
This is a zanni dalala, but sufficient for the ruling.
4
Note the Hanafi reliance
The Hanafi school adopts this position as the mufta bihi. Some other schools may require a judge's verification, but Hanafis do not when both come together.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۴۱] (۱۱۶) اور اگر دونوں ساتھ قید ہوئے تو بینونت واقع نہیں ہوگی۔
وان سبيا معا لم تقع البينونة
اگر میاں بیوی دونوں ساتھ قید ہو کر دار الحرب سے دار الاسلام آئے ہوں تو دونوں کا نکاح نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔
حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) جانتا ہے۔ پس اگر ان کو جانو کہ مومنہ ہیں تو کفار کی طرف مت لوٹاؤ۔ یہ ان کے لئے حلال نہیں اور وہ ان کے لئے حلال نہیں۔ اور جو کچھ کفار نے خرچ کیا ہے اس کو دیدو۔ اور تم پر کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کہ نکاح کرو اگر ان کو ان کا مہر دیدو۔ اور کافروں کا دامن مت تھا مو ( الف ) حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں اگر نصرانیہ شوہر سے ایک گھنٹہ پہلے مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس پر حرام ہو جائے گی۔ حضرت عطاء سے ذمی عورت کے بارے میں پوچھا کہ وہ اسلام لے آئی پھر اس کا شوہر عدت میں مسلمان ہوا تو کیا وہ اس کی بیوی رہی؟ فرمایا نہیں مگر یہ کہ نئے نکاح اور نئے مہر سے چاہے (ب) آپ نے منع فرمایا کہ صحبت کرے حاملہ عورت سے یہاں تک کہ بچہ جن دے۔ یا غیر حاملہ سے یہاں تک کہ ایک حیض آجائے۔
If both are captured together, separation does not occur.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that if both spouses are taken captive together and brought to Dar al-Islam, their marriage remains valid. The reason is that ikhtilaf al-dar does not occur since both are now in the same abode. The commentary references the Quranic verse about not returning believing women to disbelievers, which implies that if both are in Dar al-Islam, no separation is needed. The athar of Ibn Abbas and the hadith about captives are also cited to show that the marriage remains intact. The principle is that the mutual union is preserved as long as the spouses are together, and there is no impediment.

Key Terms
معا (ma'an): Together, both at the same time.
بينونة (baynuna): Separation, dissolution of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband and wife are both captured and brought to Dar al-Islam together, what happens to their marriage according to the Hanafi school?
A) Their marriage is automatically dissolved.
B) Their marriage remains valid.
C) Their marriage becomes suspended until they both convert.
D) They must renew their marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
When both spouses are captured together, their marriage continues; separation only occurs when they end up in different abodes.

A Migrant Woman May Remarry Immediately Without Iddah
Ruling that a migrant woman may remarry without iddah, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that a woman migrating from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam may remarry without iddah, and evaluate the counter-argument of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A migrant woman from Dar al-Harb may remarry immediately because iddah honors a husband who deserves no honor.

This lesson examines a classical dispute within the Hanafi school: whether a woman who migrates alone from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam must observe a waiting period (iddah) before remarrying. Imam Abu Hanifa held that she may marry immediately, while his two main disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) required iddah. The disagreement turns on the purpose of iddah and the status of a harbi husband. By analyzing the evidence, you will see how Hanafi usul principles determine the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
What does the text say about the migrant woman? She may marry immediately with no iddah according to Abu Hanifa.
The text explicitly states 'جاز لها أن تتزوج في الحال فلا عدة عليها عند أبي حنيفة'.
2
Analyze the Proof
What is the primary dalil? Quran 60:10, which permits marriage immediately after giving mahr, implying no waiting period.
The verse says: ولا جناح عليكم أن تنكحوهن إذا آتيتموهن أجورهن (There is no sin for you to marry them when you have given them their dowers).
3
Understand the Rationale
Why does Abu Hanifa say no iddah? Because iddah honors the previous husband, and a harbi husband has no honor in Islam.
The text explains: عدت پہلے شوہر کے احترام کے لئے ہے اور پہلا شوہر کافر حربی ہے اس لئے اس کا کوئی احترام نہیں ہے.
4
Examine the Dispute
What do the Sahibayn argue? That once in Dar al-Islam, she is subject to Islamic law which requires iddah for all women whose marriages are dissolved.
The text states: صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر عدت ہے کیونکہ وہ دار الاسلام میں آگئی ہے۔
5
Determine the Operational Ruling
Which position is mufta bihi according to this text? The text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon position.
The fatwa in the Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa, as indicated by the presentation of his view first as the correct one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۴۲] (۱۷۷) إذا خرجت المرأة الينا مهاجرة جاز لها أن تتزوج في الحال فلا عدة عليها عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى
واذا خرجت المرأة الينا مهاجرة جاز لها ان تتزوج في الحال فلا عدة عليها عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى
[۱۸۴۲] (۱۷۷) اگر عورت دار الاسلام کی طرف ہجرت کر کے آئی تو اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ فی الحال شادی کرے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر عدت نہیں ہے۔
آیت میں ہے ولا جناح عليكم ان تنكحوا من اذا آتيتموهن أجورهن ولا تمسكو بعصم الكوافر (آية ۱۰ سورة الممتحنة (۶۰) ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ مہر ادا کرو تو مہاجرہ عورت سے شادی کر سکتے ہو ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فوری طور پر اس سے شادی کر سکتا ہے (۲) یہ عورت ہجرت کر کے دار الاسلام آئی ہے۔ یہاں اس کا کوئی ذی رحم محرم نہیں ہو گا اس لئے یہ اگر شادی کر کے شوہر نہ بنائے تو کیسے اجنبی کے پاس رہے گی۔ اس لئے شریعت نے عدت گزارے بغیر شادی کو جائز قرار دیا (۳) عدت پہلے شوہر کے احترام کے لئے ہے۔ اور پہلا شوہر کا فر اور حربی ہے اس لئے اس کا کوئی احترام نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ایسی عورت پر عدت بھی نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر عدت ہے ۔ کیونکہ وہ دار الاسلام میں آگئی ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر دار الاسلام کا حکم لازم ہوگا۔ اور دار الاسلام کا حکم یہ ہے کہ مطلقہ اور تفریق شدہ عورت پر عدت لازم ہوتی ہے۔ حدیث اوپر گزر گئی ہے ( دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح، ج ثالث ،ص ۱۸۰ نمبر ۳۳۵۹۸)
If a woman comes to us as a migrant, it is permissible for her to marry immediately, and there is no iddah upon her according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a woman who migrates alone from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam may remarry immediately without observing any iddah. The proof is the Quranic verse 'There is no sin for you to marry them when you have given them their dowers' (60:10), which implies immediate permission. The reasoning is that iddah is to honor the former husband, but a kafir harbi has no honor. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, saying that once she is in Dar al-Islam, she is subject to Islamic law, which requires iddah for divorced or separated women. The relied upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Imam Abu Hanifa according to this text.

Key Terms
مهاجرة (muhajirah): A woman who migrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam, leaving her non-Muslim husband behind.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling for a woman who migrates alone from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam regarding iddah?
A) She must observe iddah for three months.
B) She must observe iddah for one menstrual cycle.
C) She may remarry immediately with no iddah.
D) She may never remarry because her previous marriage is permanent.

Key Takeaway
A woman migrating from Dar al-Harb may remarry immediately without iddah because a harbi husband's honor is not recognized in Islamic law.

intermediate

Ruling on 'Iddah for Female Migrant to Dar al-Islam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'iddah for migrant woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on 'iddah for a migrant woman, explain his proof from Quran 60:10, and compare it with the Sahibayn's position, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A migrant woman from Dar al-Harb may remarry immediately without 'iddah according to Abu Hanifa, because her previous husband, a kafir harbi, deserves no respect.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: the waiting period ('iddah) for a woman who migrates from a non-Muslim land (Dar al-Harb) to a Muslim land (Dar al-Islam), leaving her non-Muslim husband. Abu Hanifa holds that no 'iddah is required, allowing immediate remarriage, while his two principal disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), insist on the standard 'iddah. The dispute hinges on the interpretation of Quran 60:10 and the general principles of 'iddah. By studying this, you will appreciate how Hanafi scholars derive rulings from primary texts and how legitimate differences coexist within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the act under dispute? Here, it is whether a woman who migrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam must observe 'iddah (a waiting period) after separation from her non-Muslim husband before she can remarry.
The dispute is only about the 'iddah; the marriage is considered dissolved due to difference of abode (ikhtilaf al-darin).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his primary evidence
Abu Hanifa says no 'iddah is required; she may remarry immediately. His primary evidence is the Qur'anic verse (Surah al-Mumtahina 60:10), which permits marrying migrant women without mentioning an 'iddah. He also uses the rationale that the previous husband, being a kafir harbi, deserves no honor.
The verse is 'There is no sin upon you that you marry them when you have given them their dowries' – silence on 'iddah indicates it is not required.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their evidence
The Sahibayn hold that 'iddah is required because the woman is now in Dar al-Islam, so the general rule applies: any divorced or separated woman must observe 'iddah. They rely on general principles and a hadith (from Dar Qutni).
They argue that abode determines legal status; since she is in Dar al-Islam, the laws of Dar al-Islam apply.
4
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference is when she can remarry. Abu Hanifa: immediately after migration (if not pregnant). Sahibayn: after completing 'iddah (three menstrual cycles or three months).
This affects actual marriage arrangements and the rights of the new husband.
5
Note the absence of explicit tarjih and the cautionary approach
The text presents both views without explicitly preferring one. In later Hanafi fatwa, the cautious position (Sahibayn) is often followed to avoid potential violation of 'iddah, but the difference remains.
Muftis should be aware of both opinions and may choose based on circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معا لم تقع البينونة واذا خرجت المرأة الينا مهاجرة جاز لها ان تتزوج في الحال فلا عدة عليها عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى [ ۱۸۴۳] (۱۱۸) فان كانت حاملا لم تتزوج حتى تضع حملها.
اختلاف دارین نہیں ہوا (۲) ساتھ ہیں اس لئے بیوی اور شوہر کی مصلحت باقی ہے کہ محبت کر سکتا ہے اس لئے نکاح توڑنے سے فائدہ نہیں ہے (۳) جس طرح کسی کی باندی ہو اور اس کی شادی کسی مرد سے کرا دی جائے تو آقا کی باندی رہتے ہوئے شوہر سے استفادہ کر سکتی ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں آقا کی باندی رہتے ہوئے شوہر سے استفادہ کرے گی۔ اس لئے نکاح تو ڑوانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ ۱۸۴۲] (۱۷۷) اگر عورت دار الاسلام کی طرف ہجرت کر کے آئی تو اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ فی الحال شادی کرے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر عدت نہیں ہے۔
آیت میں ہے ولا جناح عليكم ان تنكحوا من اذا آتيتموهن أجورهن ولا تمسكو بعصم الكوافر (الف) (آيت ۰ ۱ سورۃ الترویہ (۶۰) اس آیت میں ہے کہ مہر ادا کرو تو مہاجرہ عورت سے شادی کر سکتے ہو ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فوری طور پر اس سے شادی کر سکتا ہے (۲) یہ عورت ہجرت کر کے دار الاسلام آئی ہے۔ یہاں اس کا کوئی ذی رحم محرم نہیں ہو گا اس لئے یہ اگر شادی کر کے شوہر نہ بنائے تو کیسے اجنبی کے پاس رہے گی۔ اس لئے شریعت نے عدت گزارے بغیر شادی کو جائز قرار دیا (۳) عدت پہلے شوہر کے احترام کے لئے ہے۔ اور پہلا شوہر کا فر اور حربی ہے اس لئے اس کا کوئی احترام نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ایسی عورت پر عدت بھی نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر عدت ہے ۔ کیونکہ وہ دار الاسلام میں آگئی ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر دار الاسلام کا حکم لازم ہوگا۔ اور دار الاسلام کا حکم یہ ہے کہ مطلقہ اور تفریق شدہ عورت پر عدت لازم ہوتی ہے۔ حدیث اوپر گزر گئی ہے ( دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح، ج ثالث ،ص ۱۸۰ نمبر ۳۳۵۹۸)
Even if separation does not occur, and if a woman comes to us as a migrant, it is permissible for her to marry immediately, and there is no 'iddah upon her according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. [18343] (118) If she is pregnant, she should not marry until she delivers. 
There is no difference of the two abodes [explanation in Urdu]... The verse says: 'There is no sin upon you that you marry them when you have given them their dowries, and do not hold fast to the ties of disbelieving women' (Surah al-Mumtahina 60:10). This verse indicates that you may marry a migrant woman immediately upon giving her dowry. (2) This woman has migrated to Dar al-Islam; she has no relative here, so if she does not marry, how will she stay with a stranger? Therefore, the Shari'ah permitted marriage without observing 'iddah. (3) 'Iddah is for the honor of the previous husband, and he is a kafir harbi, so he has no honor. Hence, there is no 'iddah upon such a woman. The Sahibayn say that there is 'iddah upon her because she has entered Dar al-Islam, so the ruling of Dar al-Islam applies to her, which requires 'iddah for a divorced or separated woman. The hadith has passed above (Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 3, p. 180, no. 33598).
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the 'iddah of a woman who migrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that she may remarry immediately with no 'iddah, based on the Quranic verse from Surah al-Mumtahina, which permits marriage to migrant women without mentioning 'iddah, and the rationale that her previous husband, being a harbi (enemy combatant) and kafir, deserves no respect. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) disagree, stating that since she is now in Dar al-Islam, she must observe 'iddah like any other woman divorced or separated in Dar al-Islam. They rely on the general rule that 'iddah is required for all separations occurring in Dar al-Islam. The passage also discusses a hypothetical regarding a female slave, but that is part of the commentary. The authority weight for Abu Hanifa's position is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, though the text does not explicitly state the mufta bihi; later practice tends to follow the Sahibayn for caution. The passage also notes that if the woman is pregnant, she cannot remarry until delivery—this is a separate ruling that will be covered in the next lesson.

Key Terms
عدة (‘iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or separation before remarriage, to ensure no pregnancy from the previous husband.
مهاجرة (muhājirah): A woman who migrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam, leaving her non-Muslim husband behind.
صاحبين (ṣāḥibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two major disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is there no 'iddah for a woman migrating from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam?
A) Because she is still married to her previous husband.
B) Because her previous husband is a kafir harbi, so he deserves no respect.
C) Because she is not in her menstrual period.
D) Because the Sahibayn agree with Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
According to Abu Hanifa, a woman migrating from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam may remarry immediately without 'iddah, based on Quran 60:10 and the lack of honor for her previous kafir harbi husband; the Sahibayn require 'iddah, applying the general rule.

Ruling for Pregnant Migrant Woman
Ruling on intercourse prohibition for pregnant migrant woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a pregnant migrant woman regarding remarriage and intercourse, and identify the evidence.

Core Idea
Intercourse with a pregnant migrant woman is haram until delivery, but marriage contract is allowed.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a woman who migrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam while pregnant from her previous husband. The text clarifies that although she may contract a new marriage, she cannot consummate it until she gives birth. This ruling is based on a prophetic hadith and aims to prevent confusion of lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled
What is the specific act under consideration? It is intercourse by a new husband with a pregnant woman who has migrated from Dar al-Harb.
The woman is pregnant from her previous husband, not from the new one.
2
Determine the ruling
Is the act permissible or forbidden? The text states that intercourse is prohibited until she delivers. However, the marriage contract itself is allowed.
The phrase 'lam tatazawwaj' is interpreted as referring to intercourse, not the contract.
3
Locate the evidence
What is the proof? The hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the captives of Awtas: 'A pregnant woman should not be approached until she delivers.'
This is a sahih hadith, cited in Sunan Dar Qutni and others.
4
Understand the rationale
Why is it prohibited? To avoid confusion of lineage: the child belongs to the first husband, and intercourse by the second could mix lines.
The metaphor 'irrigating the first husband's field' is used in the commentary.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the woman can marry immediately but must wait until delivery for consummation.
This distinguishes between the validity of the contract and the permissibility of intercourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كانت حاملا لم تتزوج حتى تضع حملها.
دار الحرب سے ہجرت کر کے دارالاسلام آنے والی عورت پہلے شوہر سے حاملہ ہے تو حمل کی حالت میں شادی تو کر سکتی ہے لیکن محبت نہ کرائے۔ کیونکہ پہلے شوہر کا حمل موجود ہے تو دوسرے شوہر سے صحبت کرانے سے دوسرے آدمی سے پہلے کی کھیتی کو سیراب کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ اور پتہ نہیں چلے گا کہ کس کا بچہ ہے۔ اس لئے حمل جننے تک نئے شوہر سے محبت نہ کرائے (۲) او پر حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ عـــن ابـــی ســعيــد الخدري رفعه انه قال في سبايا اوطاس لا توطأ حامل حتى تضع ولا غير ذات حمل حتى تحيض حيضة (ب)(سنن حاشیہ : (ب) تم پر کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کہ مہاجرہ عورتوں سے نکاح کرو جب ان کو ان کا مہر دو۔ اور کافروں کا دامن مت تھا مو (ب ) جنگ اوطاس کے قیدیوں کے بارے میں آپ نے فرمایا حاملہ سے صحبت مت کرو یہاں تک کہ بچہ جن دے۔ اور غیر حاملہ سے جب تک ایک حیض نہ آجائے۔
If she is pregnant, she should not marry until she delivers.
A woman who migrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam and is pregnant from the previous husband may contract marriage while pregnant, but she should not have intercourse until delivery. Because the pregnancy from the first husband exists, and having intercourse with the second husband would mean irrigating the first husband's field with the second man's water, and it would be unclear whose child it is. Therefore, she should not have intercourse with the new husband until she delivers. (2) The hadith has passed above: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, marfu'an, that he said regarding the captives of Awtas: 'A pregnant woman should not be approached until she delivers, and a non-pregnant woman should not be approached until she has one menstruation.' (Sunan, footnote: (b) 'There is no sin upon you that you marry them when you have given them their dowries, and do not hold fast to the ties of disbelieving women.' (Quran 60:10) (b) Regarding the captives of Awtas, the Prophet said: 'Do not have intercourse with a pregnant woman until she gives birth, and with a non-pregnant woman until she has one menstruation.')
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This lesson states a ruling for a pregnant migrant woman. While a non-pregnant migrant woman may remarry immediately (per Abu Hanifa), a pregnant one must wait until delivery before she can have intercourse with the new husband. The prohibition is based on the hadith of the Prophet about the captives of Awtas, which forbids intercourse with a pregnant woman until she delivers. The reason is to avoid confusion of lineage and to protect the previous husband's child. Note that the ruling says 'lam tatazawwaj' meaning she should not have intercourse (not necessarily that she cannot contract marriage). The commentary clarifies that she can still contract the marriage, but cannot consummate until delivery. This is consistent with the principle that a pregnant woman can be married but intercourse is prohibited until delivery.

Key Terms
حامل (ḥāmil): A pregnant woman, in this context, a woman who is pregnant from her previous marriage before migration.
وضع حمل (waḍʿ ḥaml): The act of giving birth; the termination of pregnancy by delivery.
وطء (waṭʾ): Sexual intercourse, used in the hadith to refer to the prohibition of approaching a pregnant woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) After three months.

Key Takeaway
A pregnant migrant woman may contract marriage but intercourse is haram until she delivers, to protect lineage.

Apostasy of a Spouse: Faskh or Talaq? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on immediate separation and mahr consequences when a spouse apostatizes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether apostasy causes faskh or talaq, identify the evidence for each view, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Apostasy dissolves marriage immediately but is faskh, not talaq, according to Abu Hanifa.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute: what is the legal nature of the marriage breakdown when a spouse apostatizes? The majority of the Hanafi school, following Imam Abu Hanifa, holds that it is an annulment (faskh) of the marriage contract, not a divorce (talaq). However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that it should be treated as an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain). Understanding this difference is critical for determining the wife's right to mahr, the effect on the husband's remaining divorces, and the legal remedies available to the couple.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
State the Hanafi position that apostasy by either spouse immediately dissolves the marriage. Then identify the two views within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa says it is faskh; Imam Muhammad says it is talaq bain.
2
Examine the Evidence for Each View
List the proofs: Abu Hanifa cites Quran 60:10, an athar from Ibn Abbas, and an athar from 'Ata'. Imam Muhammad cites athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i stating that any separation initiated by the husband is talaq or talaq bain.
Both sides use athar, so the dispute is over interpretation and weight.
3
Analyze the Legal Basis (Ta'lil)
Understand the reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues that apostasy shows disrespect, whereas talaq implies respect; thus apostasy cannot be talaq. Imam Muhammad argues that because the husband initiates the separation, it must be a form of talaq.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Compare the practical consequences: Under faskh, the separation does not reduce the husband's number of permissible divorces; under talaq bain, it counts as one divorce. Also, the 'iddah and mahr implications differ slightly.
In both cases, the wife is entitled to full mahr if consummated, half if not.
5
Identify the Mufta Bihi Position
Conclude that the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view: apostasy causes faskh, not talaq. This is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is followed by later authorities such as al-Hidayah.
Imam Muhammad's view is a nawadir position but not the mufta bihi.

Source Text

واذا ارتد احد الزوجين عن الاسلام وقعت البينونة بينهما وكانت الفرقة بينهما بغير طلاق فان كان الزوج هو المرتد وقد دخل بها فلها : للبیہقی ، باب استبراء من ملک الامته ج سابع ص ۳۳۹ ردار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۱۸۰ نمبر ۳۵۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حاملہ عورت سے وضع حمل سے پہلے صحبت نہ کرے۔

امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر مرتد ہوا ہے جس کی وجہ سے فرقت ہوتی ہے تو چونکہ شوہر کی جانب سے فرقت کی ابتدا ہوئی اس لئے وہ طلاق کے درجے میں ہوگی (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال كل فرقة كانت من قبل الرجل فهي طلاق (و) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۸۹ من قال كل فرقته تطلیقہ ج رابع ، ص ۱۱۳، نمبر ۱۸۳۳۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اگر شوہر کی جانب سے فرقت ہوئی ہو تو وہ طلاق شمار ہوگی۔ اور دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال كل فرقة فهى تطليقة بائن (و) ( رابع ص ۱۱۳ نمبر ۱۸۳۴۰) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ طلاق بائنہ ہوگی۔ [ ۱۸۴۵) (۱۲۰) پس اگرشو ہر مرتد ہوا ہو اور اس سے صحبت کر چکا ہو تو عورت کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا۔ اور اگر محبت نہ کی ہو تو اس کے لئے آدھا مہر پورا اوراگر اس حاشیہ : (الف) نہ مومنہ عورتیں مشرک کے لئے حلال ہیں اور نہ مشرک مردان عورتوں کے لئے حلال ہیں (ب) حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر نصرانیہ عورت شوہر سے ایک گھنٹہ پہلے مسلمان ہو جائے تو وہ اس پر حرام ہو جائے گی (ج) حضرت عطاء نے فرمایا نصرانیہ عورت شوہر کے تحت مسلمان ہو جائے، فرمایا تفریق ہو جائے گی (1) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا ہر تفریق جو مرد کی جانب سے ہو وہ طلاق ہے (ہ) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا ہر تفریق وہ طلاق بائنہ ہے۔
If one of the spouses apostatizes from Islam, separation occurs between them, and the separation is without talaq. If the husband is the apostate and has consummated, then she gets [the full mahr...] (hadith references)... This hadith states that one should not have intercourse with a pregnant woman before delivery. The meaning of 'lam tatazawwaj' is that she should not have intercourse, but she may contract marriage. [1844] (119) If one of the spouses apostatizes from Islam, separation (bainunah) occurs between them, and the separation is without talaq. If either spouse becomes apostate, immediately separation occurs. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this separation is considered faskh of the marriage. The reason the marriage breaks immediately is because he has become a kafir, and marriage of a kafir with a Muslim is not valid. Moreover, he apostatized after Islam and after understanding everything, so he is a worse kafir. Therefore, his marriage breaks immediately. (2) The verse says: 'They are not lawful to them, nor are they lawful to them' (Surah al-Mumtahina 60:10). (3) From Ibn Abbas: 'If a Christian woman becomes Muslim an hour before her husband, she becomes forbidden to him' (Bukhari). Similarly, if a Muslim becomes apostate, he becomes forbidden to his wife. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this separation is not talaq because in apostasy there is no respect, and making it talaq is a sign of respect. Therefore, it is faskh. (2) There is an athar from 'Ata': 'Regarding a Christian woman who becomes Muslim while under her husband, he said: separation is made between them.' This means separation occurs, not talaq. Imam Muhammad says: If the husband apostatizes and separation occurs, since the husband initiated the separation, it is in the category of talaq. (2) There is an athar from Ibrahim: 'Every separation that comes from the man is talaq' (Ibn Abi Shaybah). And another: 'Every separation is a talaq bain.' So it is known that it is talaq bain. [1845] (120) Then if the husband is the apostate and has consummated, then she gets the full mahr. If he did not consummate, she gets half the mahr... [text cut off]
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal consequences of apostasy by one spouse. There is a consensus that the marriage is immediately dissolved, but a dispute exists as to whether this dissolution is faskh (annulment) or talaq (divorce). Imam Abu Hanifa holds it is faskh, not talaq, because apostasy shows contempt and lacks the respect required for talaq. He cites the Quranic verse 60:10 and an athar from Ibn Abbas. Imam Muhammad, however, argues that since the husband causes the separation, it should be treated as talaq bain, relying on athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. The practical difference: if it is faskh, the husband cannot take her back except with a new marriage; if it is talaq bain, similar effect but technically counts as a divorce. The passage also details the mahr consequences: if consummated, full mahr; if not, half mahr (standard rule for separation due to apostasy). The OCR ends mid-sentence, but the ruling is clear. The authority weight for Abu Hanifa's view is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, though the later school often adopts the view that apostasy causes faskh, not talaq.

Key Terms
ارتداد (irtidād): Apostasy from Islam; leaving the Islamic faith.
بينونة (baynūna): Complete separation; legal disunion of spouses.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract due to a defect or supervening cause.
طلاق (ṭalāq): Divorce initiated by the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the legal nature of the separation caused by apostasy of the husband?
A) It is a talaq bain (irrevocable divorce).
B) It is a faskh (annulment) of the marriage.
C) It is a talaq raj'i (revocable divorce).
D) It does not dissolve the marriage.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy by a spouse instantly dissolves the marriage as faskh (annulment) in the Hanafi school, a distinction that determines mahr obligations and the husband's divorce count.

Mahr Entitlement Upon Husband's Apostasy
Ruling on wife's mahr upon husband's apostasy, with two scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wife's mahr entitlement when the husband apostatizes, distinguishing between consummated and unconsummated marriages, and apply the underlying analogy to divorce.

Core Idea
Apostasy of the husband after consummation entitles the wife to full mahr; before consummation, only half.

What happens to the wife's mahr when the husband leaves Islam? The Hanafi school provides a clear rule based on whether the marriage was consummated. This lesson walks through the two branches of the ruling and the legal reasoning — an analogy to divorce — so you can confidently determine the wife's entitlement in this scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause of separation
The marriage ends due to the husband's apostasy (irtidad). This is a separation initiated by the husband.
Apostasy invalidates the marriage immediately in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Apply the ruling for a consummated marriage
If the husband had sexual intercourse (dukhul) with his wife, she is entitled to the full mahr.
Consummation perfects the mahr obligation.
3
Apply the ruling for an unconsummated marriage
If the marriage was not consummated, the wife receives only half the mahr.
This is identical to the rule for divorce before consummation.
4
Recognize the underlying legal principle
The ruling is based on an analogy (qiyas) to talaq before consummation: separation by the husband without the wife's fault results in half mahr; full mahr requires consummation.
The same 'illa (effective cause) applies: the husband terminates the marriage before consummation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كان الزوج هو المرتد وقد دخل بها فلها المهر كاملا وان لم يدخل بها فلها نصف المهر
پس اگر شوہر مرتد ہوا ہو اور اس سے صحبت کر چکا ہو تو عورت کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا۔ اور اگر صحبت نہ کی ہو تو اس کے لئے آدھا مہر ہوگا۔
Then if the husband is the apostate and he had intercourse with her, then she has the full mahr; and if he did not have intercourse with her, then she has half the mahr. So if the husband became an apostate and he had intercourse with her, then the woman gets the full mahr. And if he did not have intercourse, then she gets half the mahr.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for the case when the husband apostatizes. If the marriage was consummated (dukhul), the wife is entitled to the full mahr (sadaq). If it was not consummated, she receives half the mahr. The sharh explains the reason: since the separation is caused by the husband's apostasy, it is analogous to a divorce before consummation, where half the mahr is due. In the case of consummation, the full mahr is established. This ruling is consistent with the general principle that mahr becomes fully due upon valid retirement (khalwah sahihah) or actual intercourse.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): Mandatory bridal gift given by husband to wife, fully due upon consummation or valid retirement.
ارتداد (irtidad): Renunciation of Islam by a Muslim, which invalidates the marriage in Hanafi fiqh.
دخول (dukhul): Actual sexual intercourse between spouses, which perfects the mahr obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the husband apostatizes before consummation, what is the wife entitled to?
A) Full mahr
B) Half mahr
C) No mahr
D) One-third mahr

Key Takeaway
Upon husband's apostasy, wife's mahr entitlement depends solely on consummation: full if consummated, half if not.

Mahr When the Wife Apostatizes
Ruling on mahr when wife apostatizes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when the wife apostatizes and distinguish it from the husband's case.

Core Idea
When the wife apostatizes, mahr is forfeited if before consummation; if after, it is fully due.

In Hanafi fiqh, the entitlement to mahr upon separation due to apostasy depends on two factors: who caused the separation (the husband or the wife) and whether consummation occurred. This lesson focuses on the case where the wife apostatizes. The ruling draws on the precedent of Sufyan al-Thawri and is consistent across the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: apostasy before consummation and apostasy after consummation. Identify the act (wife's apostasy) and the ruling for each.
The act is the wife leaving Islam while in a valid marriage.
2
State the ruling for each case
Before consummation: no mahr. After consummation: full mahr.
These are the mufta bihi positions.
3
Locate the dalil
The passage cites the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri. Identify it as a qawl sahabi (actually tabi'i) and understand that his explicit differentiation supports the ruling.
The proof is a transmitted athar, considered reliable in Hanafi sources.
4
Contrast with husband's apostasy
The commentary notes that if the husband apostatizes before consummation, she gets half mahr. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: the difference arises because the husband caused the separation (so he must pay half), while the wife caused it (so she forfeits).
This distinction is critical for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانت المرأة هي المرتدة فان كان قبل الدخول فلا مهر لها وان كانت الردة بعد الدخول فلها المهر
اور اگر مرتد ہونا صحبت کے بعد ہوا ہو تو عورت کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا۔
حاشیہ : (ج) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا اگر عورت مرتد ہو جائے اور اس کا شوہر ہو اور صحبت نہ کی ہو تو مہر نہیں ملے گا۔ اور نکاح ٹوٹ گیا اور صحبت کر چکا ہو تو اس کو پورا مہر ملے گا۔
And if the woman is the apostate, then if it was before consummation, she has no mahr; and if the apostasy was after consummation, she has the mahr. And if apostasy occurs after intercourse, then the woman gets the full mahr. Footnote: (j) Sufyan al-Thawri said: If a woman becomes an apostate and she has a husband and he did not have intercourse with her, then she does not get a mahr, and the marriage is broken; but if he had intercourse, then she gets the full mahr.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage covers the case when the wife apostatizes. If the marriage was not consummated, the wife is not entitled to any mahr because she caused the separation and has not yet given anything in return. If consummation occurred, she receives the full mahr because the mahr became owing upon consummation. The sharh cites the athar of Sufyan al-Thawri as evidence. The commentary also notes that when the husband is the apostate, she gets half mahr before consummation, but when the wife apostatizes, she gets nothing. The difference is that the husband caused the separation in the former case, so he must pay half, while in the latter the wife caused it, so she forfeits the mahr.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): Mandatory bridal gift; fully due upon consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the wife apostatizes before consummation, what is her mahr entitlement?
A) Full mahr
B) Half mahr
C) No mahr
D) One-quarter mahr

Key Takeaway
The wife's apostasy forfeits mahr before consummation but not after, because consummation vests the full mahr and the fault principle governs pre-consumption separation.

Both Apostatize Together Then Revert Together
Ruling with proof from Ijma of Companions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when both spouses apostatize together and revert together, and explain the proof from the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Simultaneous apostasy and return suspend then revive the marriage without renewal.

Apostasy (irtidad) is a serious matter in Islamic law, often affecting marital bonds. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between the individual and joint apostasy of spouses. This lesson examines the specific case where both spouses leave Islam together and later return together. The ruling, rooted in the precedent of the Companions, preserves the original marriage contract, highlighting the principle that simultaneous actions can nullify the disruptive effect of apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
First, pinpoint the scenario: both spouses apostatize at the same time, then both revert to Islam at the same time. The ruling is that their marriage remains valid (sahih) without needing a new contract.
The key is the simultaneity of both acts.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the practice of the Companions during the caliphate of Abu Bakr with the Banu Hanifa tribe. They apostatized en masse and later returned en masse, and the Companions did not renew their marriages.
This is an example of Ijma (consensus) of the Companions.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The legal link: the Companions' inaction (not renewing contracts) indicates that the marriage was not considered dissolved. Therefore, simultaneous apostasy and return suspends but does not nullify the marriage; it revives upon return.
The ruling is derived from the absence of action, which carries legal weight.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
There is no significant disagreement within the Hanafi school on this point, and it is considered muttafaq alayh (agreed upon) across schools. Some other schools might require renewal if apostasy involved a change in religion, but the Hanafi position is based on the specific precedent.
This ruling is distinct from cases where only one spouse apostatizes.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The ruling is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) and relies on the strength of the Companions' consensus, which is a primary source of law in the Hanafi school.
No later tarjih is needed as the ruling is clear and widely accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ارتدا معا ثم أسلما معا فهما على نكاحهما
بنی حنیفہ کے لوگ حضرت ابو بکر کے زمانے میں ایک ساتھ مرتد ہوئے تھے اور ایک ساتھ مسلمان ہوئے تھے تو صحابہ نے کسی کا نکاح دوبارہ نہیں پڑھایا بلکہ پہلے نکاح پر بحال رکھا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دونوں ایک ساتھ مرتد ہوئے ہوں اور ایک ساتھ مسلمان ہوئے ہوں تو نکاح بحال رہے گا۔
And if they both apostatize together, then both become Muslim together, they remain on their marriage. The people of Banu Hanifa in the time of Abu Bakr apostatized together and became Muslim together, and the Companions did not have their marriage renewed, but rather kept them on their original marriage. From this it is known that if both apostatize together and become Muslim together, the marriage remains valid.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where both spouses apostatize simultaneously and later simultaneously return to Islam. The ruling is that their marriage continues as before, without needing a new marriage contract. The sharh supports this by citing the historical precedent of the Banu Hanifa tribe during the caliphate of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. The tribe committed apostasy en masse and later returned to Islam. The Companions did not require them to renew their marriages, establishing that simultaneous apostasy and return preserves the marriage. This is because during the period of apostasy, the marriage was suspended (not dissolved), and upon mutual return to Islam, it is revived.

Key Terms
ارتداد (irtidad): Apostasy from Islam; leaving the religion.
نكاح (nikah): Marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If both spouses apostatize together and later revert to Islam together, what is the status of their marriage?
A) The marriage is dissolved and must be renewed.
B) The marriage remains intact without renewal.
C) The marriage is dissolved but they can remarry without new mahr.
D) The marriage is suspended until one of them returns to Islam.

Key Takeaway
Simultaneous apostasy and return of both spouses preserves the original marriage contract without renewal.

Marriage Restrictions for an Apostate
Ruling on whom an apostate may marry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on marriage for an apostate and identify the reason for the prohibition.

Core Idea
An apostate cannot marry anyone until they return to Islam.

This passage from the matn explicitly forbids an apostate from contracting any marriage. The prohibition is absolute and applies to both male and female apostates. Understanding this ruling clarifies the strict boundary Islam places on marriage with apostates, based on the principle that a Muslim cannot marry a disbeliever.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the subject
The act is marriage (nikah), and the subject is an apostate (murtadd/murtaddah).
Apostasy means leaving Islam.
2
Determine the ruling (hukm)
The text says 'la yajuz' (not permissible), which in Hanafi fiqh indicates haram and the marriage is invalid.
3
Identify who is prohibited
The apostate is prohibited from marrying any Muslim woman, any apostate woman, and any disbelieving woman. Similarly, an apostate woman cannot marry any Muslim man, apostate man, or disbelieving man.
The prohibition covers all potential spouses.
4
Note the consequence
The marriage contract is invalid (batil) and must not be performed. If contracted, it must be annulled.
5
Apply the underlying principle
The principle: a Muslim cannot marry a disbeliever (Quran 60:10). An apostate is considered a disbeliever, so the marriage is forbidden.
This ruling is based on the apostate's loss of Muslim status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز ان يتزوج المرتد مسلمة ولا مرتدة ولا كافرة وكذلك
نہیں جائز ہے کہ مرتد شادی کرے کسی مسلمان عورت سے نہ مرتدہ سے نہ کافرہ سے۔ اور ایسے ہی مرتدہ عورت نہ شادی کرے کسی مسلمان سے نہ مرتد سے نہ کافر سے۔
And it is not permissible for an apostate to marry a Muslim woman, nor an apostate woman, nor a disbelieving woman; and likewise. It is not permissible for an apostate to marry any Muslim woman, nor an apostate woman, nor a disbelieving woman. And similarly, an apostate woman should not marry a Muslim nor an apostate nor a disbeliever.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage states the general prohibition on marriage for an apostate. An apostate (male or female) is not allowed to contract any valid marriage. This is because apostasy makes the person a disbeliever, and Islamic law does not permit a Muslim to marry a disbeliever (Quran 60:10). Moreover, the apostate's nikkah is invalid until they return to Islam. The sharh simply reiterates the matn, emphasizing the prohibition applies to all potential spouses: a Muslim, a fellow apostate, or any disbeliever. This ruling is based on the Quranic prohibition of marriage between Muslims and disbelievers.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who has apostatized from Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, an apostate may marry:
A) A Muslim
B) Another apostate
C) A disbeliever
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
An apostate cannot enter into any valid marriage contract until they return to Islam.

Wife's Apostasy Before Consummation: No Mahr
Ruling on mahr when wife apostatizes before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when a wife apostatizes before consummation and explain the reasoning based on the cause of separation.

Core Idea
A wife's apostasy before consummation forfeits the entire mahr because she caused the separation.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case of marriage dissolution: when the wife apostatizes before consummation. The Hanafi school rules that she receives no mahr at all. This ruling hinges on who caused the separation and whether the wife has surrendered herself physically. We will explore the textual proof and the legal reasoning behind this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
The case is when a wife apostatizes from Islam before consummation. The ruling is that she is entitled to no mahr (neither full nor half).
The ruling is conditional on apostasy occurring before dukhul.
2
Analyze the cause of separation
The text explains that the separation (firqah) is caused by the wife's own act of apostasy, not by the husband. Therefore, she does not deserve compensation.
Compare with husband-initiated divorce before consummation, where half mahr is due.
3
Examine the proof (athar)
The passage cites an athar from Sufyan al-Thawri (a mursal hadith) in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. The athar explicitly states that if a woman apostatizes before consummation, she gets no dower.
The Hanafi school acts upon this mursal narration.
4
Distinguish from other scenarios
Unlike cases where the husband divorces before consummation (half mahr) or where consummation has occurred (full mahr despite apostasy), here the wife gets nothing because she caused the dissolution.
The ruling does not apply if the husband apostatizes or if apostasy occurs after consummation.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
This ruling is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, based on the athar and the principle that fault for separation affects mahr.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement is noted for this specific ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانت المرأة هي المرتدة فان كان قبل الدخول فلا مهر لها [۱۸۴۶) (۱۲۱) اور گر عورت مرتد ہوئی ہے۔ پس اگر صحبت سے پہلے ہے تو اس کے لئے کوئی مہر نہیں ہے۔ (۱) عورت مرتد ہوئی ہے اس لئے فرقت کا سبب اس کی جانب سے ہوا ہے۔ اور اس نے مال بھی سپرد نہیں کیا ہے اس لئے اس کو آدھا عہر بھی نہیں ملے گا (۲) او پر اثر میں گزرا ہے کہ عورت مرتد ہوئی ہو اور اس سے صحبت نہ کی گئی ہو تو اس کو کچھ بھی نہیں ملے گا ( مصنف عبدالرزاق نمبر ۱۲۶۱۸)
And if the woman is the apostate, then if it was before consummation, there is no mahr for her. [1846] (121) And if the woman apostatized, so if before consummation, then there is no mahr for her. (1) The woman apostatized, therefore the cause of separation came from her side. And she did not surrender the wealth, so she does not even get half the mahr. (2) The athar passed that if the woman apostatized and consummation did not occur, then she gets nothing (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq no. 12618).
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on the mahr of a wife who apostatizes from Islam before consummation. The ruling is that she receives no mahr at all, not even half. The reasoning is twofold: first, the separation (firqah) is caused by her own act of apostasy, not by the husband; second, she has not yet surrendered herself in a way that would entitle her to compensation (since consummation is the act that makes the full mahr obligatory, and even half is only due if the husband initiates separation). The proof cited is an athar (narration) from Sufyan al-Thawri, reported in the Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq. This athar establishes the general principle that apostasy before consummation voids the mahr entirely.

Key Terms
ردة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam; the act of a Muslim abandoning the faith.
مهر (mahr): The dower or bridal gift that the husband must pay to the wife, either specified in the marriage contract or determined by law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She is entitled to half the mahr.
B) She is entitled to the full mahr.
C) She is entitled to no mahr at all.
D) It is deferred until reconciliation.

Key Takeaway
A wife's apostasy before consummation voids the mahr entirely because the separation is caused by her own act.

Wife's Apostasy After Consummation: Full Mahr
Ruling on mahr after wife's apostasy post-consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when the wife apostatizes after consummation and identify the proof from the athar of Sufyan al-Thawri.

Core Idea
Consummation makes full mahr obligatory; apostasy does not cancel earned rights.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case within marriage contracts: what happens to the mahr (dower) if the wife apostatizes after consummation. The Hanafi school, relying on the athar of Sufyan al-Thawri, holds that she retains the full mahr because the obligation crystallized at consummation. This ruling illustrates the broader principle that rights already established are not nullified by subsequent events.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Determine the key factors: wife's apostasy occurs after valid consummation (dakhul) of the marriage.
The ruling only applies if consummation happened; pre-consumption has a different rule.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The wife is entitled to the full mahr; the husband must pay it in full.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the athar of Sufyan al-Thawri recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq: 'If he has consummated with her, then she has the full dower.'
This is a mursal hadith, but accepted in Hanafi fiqh for such rulings.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly ties full dower to consummation, implying that subsequent apostasy does not affect it.
The legal principle: rights that have vested are not nullified by later events.
5
Note cross-madhhab context
Most schools agree that consummation makes full mahr obligatory, but some may consider apostasy as a ground for reduction; Hanafi holds it remains full.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the broader Islamic legal tradition.

Source Text

And if apostasy was after consummation, then she has the full mahr. [11847] (122) And if apostasy happened after consummation, then the woman has the full mahr. (1) Although the woman apostatized, she has already surrendered the wealth, so she gets the full mahr. (2) The athar of Hadrat Thawri has passed: if consummation occurred, then the woman gets the full mahr. 'For if he has consummated with her, then she has the full dower' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Murtaddin, vol. 7, p. 61, no. 12618).
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi ruling on mahr when the wife apostatizes after consummation (dakhul). The ruling is that she is entitled to the full mahr. The reason is that she has already surrendered herself to her husband (i.e., she has allowed consummation), which makes the entire mahr obligatory. Her subsequent apostasy does not cancel that obligation. The proof is again the athar of Sufyan al-Thawri, which explicitly states that if consummation has occurred, she receives the complete dower. This is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that the mahr becomes fully due upon valid consummation.

Key Terms
دخول (dakhul): Consummation of marriage; physical union between husband and wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) She forfeits all.
C) She keeps the full mahr.
D) It becomes a debt on the Muslim community.

Key Takeaway
Consummation triggers full mahr; subsequent apostasy does not void that obligation.

Prohibition of Apostate's Marriage
Ruling prohibiting apostate from marrying anyone, with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the marriage of an apostate and identify the proofs from Sunnah and Quran that support this ruling.

Core Idea
An apostate cannot marry anyone — death or imprisonment nullifies marital capacity.

This lesson addresses a specific but crucial ruling in Hanafi family law: the absolute prohibition of marriage for an apostate. The passage presents the ruling for both male and female apostates, then substantiates it with two hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and a Quranic verse (4:137). Understanding this ruling requires connecting the fiqh conclusion to its dalil, a skill essential for legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
From the text, state the exact ruling: a male apostate cannot marry any woman (Muslim, apostate, or disbeliever), and a female apostate cannot marry any man.
Note the symmetry: prohibition applies to both genders, regardless of the partner's religion.
2
Locate the primary dalil (hadith)
The author cites the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' (Bukhari). Understand how this command of execution removes the apostate's capacity for marriage.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but still authoritative for rulings.
3
Analyze the second dalil (Quran)
Verse 4:137 shows God's severe displeasure with apostates, reinforcing the worldly deprivation. Identify how this supports the prohibition.
Although the Quranic verse is qati al-thubut, its dalala is zanni; combined with hadith it strengthens the case.
4
Understand the gender difference in punishment
The male apostate is executed if he does not repent; the female apostate is imprisoned until repentance. Both punishments prevent marriage.
The underlying rationale is the same: loss of legal capacity to contract marriage.
5
Apply the ruling to hypothetical scenarios
Test your understanding: what if the apostate repents before execution? The marriage prohibition lifts because the person is no longer an apostate.
But if the apostate dies without repentance, the marriage is void ab initio.

And it is not permissible that an apostate marries a Muslim woman, nor an apostate woman, nor a disbelieving woman. Similarly, a female apostate is not married by a Muslim, nor a disbeliever, nor an apostate. [1849] (124) It is not permissible that an apostate marries any Muslim woman, nor an apostate woman, nor a disbelieving woman. And similarly, a female apostate should not marry a Muslim, nor a disbeliever, nor an apostate. After calling the male apostate to Islam, if he does not believe, he will be killed. So where is the time to give him permission to marry? (2) In hadith: the apostate is to be killed immediately. From Ikrimah: Ali brought some zanadiqah (heretics) and burned them. This reached Ibn Abbas, who said: If it were I, I would not have burned them because the Messenger of Allah forbade punishing with Allah's punishment, but I would have killed them because the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' (Bukhari, Bab hukm al-murtadd, p. 1022, no. 6922). (3) Another hadith: From Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: A man was tied up. Muadh ibn Jabal asked: What is this? They said: He was a Jew, became Muslim, then reverted to Judaism. Muadh said: Sit. He said: I will not sit until he is killed, it is the decree of Allah and His Messenger - three times. So he was ordered and killed. (Bukhari, no. 6923). So the apostate is killed; he is not given respite to marry. (4) The Quranic verse also indicates this: 'Indeed, those who have believed then disbelieved, then believed then disbelieved, and then increased in disbelief - never will Allah forgive them, nor will He guide them to a way' (4:137). In this verse, Allah has dealt severely with the apostate. And if a woman apostatizes, she will be imprisoned until she repents. Therefore she also will not have permission to go out. So she also cannot marry.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that an apostate (male) is prohibited from marrying any woman—whether Muslim, apostate, or disbeliever. Similarly, a female apostate is prohibited from marrying any man—Muslim, disbeliever, or apostate. The reasoning is twofold: (1) For the male apostate, he is called to repentance; if he does not repent, he is executed by the Islamic state. Since he faces the death penalty, he has no opportunity to marry. The proof comes from the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' (Bukhari), and the practice of the Companions. (2) For the female apostate, she is not executed but is imprisoned until she repents. Since she is confined, she cannot contract a marriage. The passage also cites a Quranic verse (4:137) showing God's severe treatment of apostates, reinforcing that the apostate is not to be given any worldly opportunity, including marriage. The ruling is clear: an apostate's marriage is invalid regardless of the spouse's religion.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A male apostate from Islam; one who abandons the Islamic faith.
مرتدة (murtaddah): A female apostate from Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A Muslim woman only.
B) An apostate woman only.
C) A Christian or Jewish woman.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
An apostate's marriage is absolutely prohibited due to the loss of legal capacity from the death penalty (male) or imprisonment (female).

Child Follows the Muslim Parent
Ruling on the religion of a child when one parent is Muslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the religion of a child when one parent is Muslim and identify the proof from the hadith of Rafi' ibn Sinan.

Core Idea
When one parent is Muslim, the child is Muslim – the better religion prevails.

This lesson addresses a fundamental question in Islamic family law: if one parent embraces Islam and the other does not, what is the religious status of their child? The Hanafi school firmly rules that the child is considered Muslim, influenced by the Muslim parent. This ruling is based on a hadith and has significant implications for the child's worldly and spiritual life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the determination of the child's religion. The ruling: the child is Muslim when one parent is Muslim.
The child is not given a choice until puberty; the affiliation is immediate.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Rafi' ibn Sinan, where the Prophet assigned the child to the Muslim father when the mother refused Islam.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for Hanafi proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's assignment indicates that the child follows the Muslim parent's religion; the child's affiliation is with the better religion.
The ruling is not based on custodianship but on religious affiliation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that the child chooses at puberty, but Hanafi holds the child is Muslim from birth.
The practical difference affects inheritance, marriage, and custody.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
The child is entitled to Islamic rights (inheritance, marriage to Muslims) and obligations (prayer, zakah) from birth.
The child is considered a Muslim in all legal matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا كان احد الزوجين مسلما فان الولد على دينه [1850] (125) اگر میاں بیوی میں سے ایک مسلمان ہو تو بچہ اس کے دین پر ہوگا۔ بچے کو مسلمان شمار کرنے سے اس کا فائدہ ہے کہ وہ آخرت میں جنت میں جائے گا اور دنیا میں اس کو دار الاسلام کی جانب سے بہت سی سہولتیں ملیں گی۔ اس لئے بچے کو والد یا والدہ جو مسلمان ہو اس کے تابع کر کے مسلمان شمار کریں گے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے بچہ مسلمان والد کو دیا ۔ عن جدی رافع بن سنان انه اسلم وابت امرأته ان تسلم فاتت النبي الله فقالت ابنتي وهي فطيم او
And if one of the spouses is Muslim, then the child follows his religion. [1850] (125) If one of the husband and wife is Muslim, the child will be on his religion. The benefit of considering the child Muslim is that he will go to Paradise in the afterlife and in the world he will get many facilities from Dar al-Islam. Therefore, the child will be made subject to the parent who is Muslim and will be considered Muslim. (2) In hadith: the Prophet assigned the child to the Muslim father. From my grandfather Rafi' ibn Sinan: he became Muslim and his wife refused to become Muslim. She came to the Prophet and said: My daughter (she was weaned or...).
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on the religious status of a child when one parent is Muslim and the other is not. The child is considered Muslim and follows the religion of the Muslim parent. The rationale is: it benefits the child spiritually (Paradise) and materially (rights in Dar al-Islam). The method is that the child is affiliated with the Muslim parent. The proof cited is a hadith from Rafi' ibn Sinan (a Companion) in which the Prophet assigned a child to the Muslim father when the mother remained non-Muslim. This shows that the Muslim parent's religion prevails over the child's religious identity. The passage also implies that the child is to be raised as a Muslim, with all attendant rights and obligations.

Key Terms
ولد (walad): Child; offspring.

Key Takeaway

Marriage with Apostates is Absolutely Prohibited
Ruling on marriage of apostates with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage involving apostates and cite the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
An apostate cannot marry anyone — the death penalty for male apostates and imprisonment for females precludes marriage entirely.

This passage establishes the Hanafi position that apostates, whether male or female, are completely barred from marriage. The ruling is derived from the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him,' and the practice of the Companions. Understanding this ruling requires recognizing the legal consequences of apostasy in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the explicit ruling: an apostate woman cannot be married by a Muslim, a non-Muslim, or another apostate. Similarly, an apostate man cannot marry a Muslim, a non-Muslim, or an apostate woman.
The ruling is absolute — no exceptions for any potential spouse.
2
Understand the rationale
The rationale is that the male apostate is to be executed if he does not repent, so he has no capacity for marriage. The female apostate is imprisoned until repentance, thus also unable to marry.
This rationale ties the marital prohibition directly to the penal consequences of apostasy.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' (Bukhari). The imperative 'faqtuluhu' indicates obligation, precluding any marriage because the apostate is to be executed.
The second hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal reinforces the immediate execution practice.
4
Note the Quranic indication
Verse 4:137 speaks of Allah's harsh treatment of apostates, supporting the severity of the ruling.
This verse is used as a supporting, not primary, evidence.
5
Apply the Hanafi position
In practice, any marriage contract involving an apostate is void. If a spouse apostatizes, the marriage is immediately invalidated.
This distinguishes Hanafi from schools that allow apostate-non-Muslim marriages.
