The Amount of Breastfeeding Causing Prohibition: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Opening ruling of Kitab al-Rada' on the effect of breastfeeding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum amount of breastfeeding that establishes marital prohibition and explain the proof from the Qur'an and hadith.

Core Idea
Any breastfeeding within the period, even a single suck, establishes prohibition—the Hanafi view based on absolute Qur'anic wording.

This lesson opens the Book of Breastfeeding (Kitab al-Rada') with a fundamental rule: both small and large amounts of breastfeeding within the legal period cause marital prohibition. This rule is disputed by Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires five distinct sessions. We will examine the Hanafi proofs, the opposing Shafi'i argument, and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its evidence
Identify the Hanafi position: any amount of breastfeeding within the period (2.5 years) creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage. The primary evidences are Qur'an 4:23 and the hadith 'Breastfeeding prohibits what birth prohibits.'
The Hanafi school argues that the Qur'anic wording is absolute and does not specify a number.
2
Identify the opposing Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that prohibition only occurs after five distinct sessions of suckling, based on a different hadith interpretation.
This is an inter-madhhab ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
3
Compare the dalil of both schools
Analyze how each school interprets the Qur'an and hadith. The Hanafi rely on the absolute command and athar from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Abbas. The Shafi'i rely on a hadith specifying five feeds.
The Hanafi response is that no specific number is mentioned in the Qur'an, and the Companion statements confirm even one suck suffices.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Hanafi, a child who suckles once becomes mahram; under Shafi'i, no prohibition unless five times. This affects marriage possibilities with the child and the woman's relatives.
5
Synthesize the tarjih
In the Hanafi madhhab, the mufta bihi position is that any amount causes prohibition, supported by the absolute proof and the practice of the Companions.
The Hanafi tarjih authority is Imam Abu Hanifa and the majority of the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرضاع
[1860] (۱) قليل الرضاع او كثيره اذا حصل في مدة الرضاع تعلق به التحريم
كتاب الرضاع
رضاعت کو دو سال کے اندر دودھ پلانے کو رضاعت کہتے ہیں۔ اس سے بھی ویسے ہی حرمت ثابت ہوتی ہے جیسے نسب سے ۔ اس آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ وامهاتكم التي ارضعنكم واخواتكم من الرضاعة (الف) (آیت ۲۳ سورۃ النساء ۴) دوسری آیت میں مدت رضاعت کا تذکرہ ہے۔ والوالدات يرضعن اولادهن حولين كاملين لمن اراد ان يتم الرضاعة (ب) (آیت ۲۳۳ سورة البقرة ٢) ان دونوں آیتوں سے رضاعت کا ثبوت ہوا۔
18۶۰] (۱) تھوڑا دودھ پلانا اور زیادہ دودھ پلانا اگر حاصل ہورضاعت کی مدت میں تو اس سے حرمت ثابت ہوگی۔ رضاعت کی مدت امام اعظم کے نزدیک ڈھائی سال ہے۔ اگر اس مدت میں عورت نے تھوڑا سا بھی بچے کو دودھ پلایا تو اس سے حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ اور اس عورت سے اس بچے کا نکاح کرنا حرام ہوگا ۔ پانچ گھونٹ پینا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ (1) حرمت کی دلیل اوپر آیت گزری و امهاتكم التي ارضعنكم واخواتكم من الرضاعة (آیت ۲۳ سورة النساء ۴) (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ ان عائشة زوج النبي الله اخبرتها ... فقال نعم الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة (ج) ( بخاری شریف باب و محرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من النسب ص ۷۶۳ نمبر ۵۰۹۹/ مسلم شریف ، باب تحرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من الولادة ص ۴۶۶ نمبر ۱۴۴۴ ترمذی شریف نمبر ۱۴۶ ابوداؤد شریف، نمبر ۲۰۵۵) اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ نسب کی وجہ سے جن عورتوں سے نکاح حرام ہے رضاعت کی وجہ سے بھی حرام ہوگا۔
اور تھوڑا سا بھی دودھ ہو اس سے حرمت ثابت ہوگی اس کی دلیل یہ ہے۔
ان عبليا وابن مسعود كانا يقولان يحرم من الرضاع قليله وكثيره (د) (نسائی شریف، القدر الذي يحرم الرضاعة ص ۴۵۷ نمبر ۱۳۳۱۳ / دار قطنی ، کتاب الرضاع ج رابع ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۴۳۱۰ رسنن للبیہقی ، باب من قال محرم قلیل الرضاع و کثیر ه ج سابع ص ۷۵۴، نمبر ۱۵۶۴۱) (۲) ان ابن عباس كان يقول ماكان في الحولين وان كانت مصة واحدة فهي تحرم (ه) موطا امام محمد، باب الرضاع ص ۲۷۶) ان آثار سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مرتبہ چوسنے سے بھی حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی (۳) آیت ارضعنکم مطلق ہے۔ کئی گھونٹ کی قید نہیں ہے اس لئے تھوڑ اسا پلانے سے بھی حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ پانچ مرتبہ بچہ دودھ چوسے گا تب حرمت ثابت ہوگی ، اس سے کم سے نہیں۔
حاشیہ : (الف) تمہاری مائیں جس نے تم کو دودھ پلایا اور تمہاری رضاعی بہن جن سے نکاح حرام ہے (ب) مائیں اپنی اولاد کو دو سال مکمل دودھ پلائیں جو مدت رضاعت پوری کرنا چاہیں ( ج ) آپ نے فرمایا ہاں ! رضاعت حرام کرتی ہے ان کو جن کو نسب کرتا ہے (1) حضرت علی اور ابن مسعود فرماتے تھے کہ حرام ہوتا ہے تھوڑا اور زیادہ دودھ پینے سے (ہ) حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ دو سال کے اندر ہو تو چاہے ایک مرتبہ چوسنا ہو وہ حرام کرتا ہے۔
Book of Breastfeeding. [1860] (1) Little or much breastfeeding, when it occurs within the period of breastfeeding, causes prohibition. Book of Breastfeeding: Breastfeeding is called rada' when milk is given within two years. It establishes the same prohibition as lineage. The proof is in the verse: 'and your mothers who gave you suck and your sisters from breastfeeding' (4:23). Another verse mentions the period: 'Mothers shall suckle their children for two whole years for those who wish to complete the breastfeeding' (2:233). Both verses prove rada'. [1860] (1) Little or much milk, if it occurs in the period of rada', establishes prohibition. The period of rada' according to Imam Abu Hanifa is two and a half years. If within this period a woman gives even a little milk to a child, prohibition is established, and marriage between that woman and the child becomes forbidden. Five sips are not necessary. (1) The proof of prohibition is the above verse 'and your mothers who gave you suck'. (2) The hadith: Aisha reported that the Prophet said, 'Yes, breastfeeding prohibits what birth prohibits.' (Bukhari, Muslim) This establishes that those women who are forbidden by lineage are also forbidden by rada'. And even a little milk establishes prohibition. The proof is that Ali and Ibn Mas'ud used to say: 'Little and much of breastfeeding prohibits.' (Nasa'i, Dar Qutni, Bayhaqi) And Ibn Abbas used to say: 'Whatever is within two years, even if it is one suck, it prohibits.' (Muwatta of Imam Muhammad) These athar show that even one suck establishes prohibition. (3) The verse 'arada'nakum' is absolute; it does not specify a number of sips, so a small amount also establishes prohibition. Imam Shafi'i says that the child must suck five times for prohibition to be established; less than that does not prohibit. Footnotes: (a) 'your mothers who gave you suck and your sisters from breastfeeding' (b) 'Mothers shall suckle... for two whole years' (c) He said, 'Yes! Breastfeeding prohibits what lineage prohibits.' (d) Ali and Ibn Mas'ud used to say that both little and much breastfeeding prohibit. (e) Ibn Abbas said that within two years, even one suck is prohibitive.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This is the introductory ruling of the Book of Breastfeeding (Kitab al-Rada'). The matn states categorically that both small and large amounts of breastfeeding, if they occur within the legal period (muddatu r-rada'), establish the same marital prohibitions (tahrim) as blood lineage. The period according to Imam Abu Hanifa is two and a half years (30 months), derived from the Qur'anic mention of two full years plus allowance for weaning. The proofs are: (1) Qur'an 4:23 listing foster mothers and sisters; (2) Qur'an 2:233 setting the period; (3) the hadith 'Breastfeeding prohibits what birth prohibits'; and (4) the statements of Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Abbas that even one suck causes prohibition. The author then notes that Imam Shafi'i differed, requiring five distinct suckling sessions for prohibition. This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position relies on the absolute wording of the Qur'an ('arada'nakum') and the general practice of the Companions. The footnotes clarify the verses and hadith.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Breastfeeding that establishes fosterage prohibition; defined as any intake of milk within the period.
حرمة (hurma): The prohibition of marriage between the nursing woman and the child, spreading to relatives as in lineage.
مدة الرضاع (muddatu r-rada'): The legal period during which breastfeeding can cause prohibition; according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is 2.5 years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Five full feedings
B) Any amount, even one suck
C) One full day of nursing
D) At least three months

Key Takeaway
Any breastfeeding within the period, even a single suck, establishes the same marital prohibitions as blood lineage in the Hanafi school.

Any Amount Establishes Prohibition: The Hanafi Position on Radāʿ
Explaining that any amount of breast milk within the period creates marital prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the quantity of breastfeeding that establishes marital prohibition and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Even a single suckle within the breastfeeding period creates the same marital prohibition as blood relations.

How much breast milk does it take to make a marriage forbidden? The Hanafi school answers: any amount at all. This lesson unpacks that ruling, examining the Qur'anic and hadith evidence that supports it, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i requirement of five separate suckles. Understanding this difference is essential for correctly determining permissible and impermissible marriages in cases of fosterage.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the quantity of breast milk needed to establish the prohibition of marriage. Note: The ruling is 'any amount within the breastfeeding period'.
The period is 30 months (Abu Hanifa) or 2 years (Sahibayn).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the Shafi'i position: marriage is not prohibited unless five distinct suckles occur.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith of Aisha regarding abrogation from ten to five suckles, and the Prophet's statement that one or two suckles do not prohibit.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand why the Hanafi school rejects the five-suckle requirement. They argue that the abrogation is not established, and the Qur'anic verse and hadith 'breastfeeding prohibits what birth prohibits' are absolute.
Also cite the athar of Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Abbas supporting one suckle.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: under Hanafi, a single suckle invalidates a marriage; under Shafi'i, less than five suckles leaves the marriage valid.
This affects fatwa and real-life marriage arrangements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۶۰] (۱) تھوڑا دودھ پلانا اور زیادہ دودھ پلانا اگر حاصل ہورضاعت کی مدت میں تو اس سے حرمت ثابت ہوگی۔ رضاعت کی مدت امام اعظم کے نزدیک ڈھائی سال ہے۔ اگر اس مدت میں عورت نے تھوڑا سا بھی بچے کو دودھ پلایا تو اس سے حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ اور اس عورت سے اس بچے کا نکاح کرنا حرام ہوگا ۔ پانچ گھونٹ پینا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ (1) حرمت کی دلیل اوپر آیت گزری و امهاتكم التي ارضعنكم واخواتكم من الرضاعة (آیت ۲۳ سورۃ النساء ۴) (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ ان عائشة زوج النبي الله اخبرتها ... فقال نعم الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة (بخاری شریف باب و محرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من النسب ص ۷۶۳ نمبر ۵۰۹۹/ مسلم شریف ، باب تحرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من الولادة ص ۴۶۶ نمبر ۱۴۴۴ ترمذی شریف نمبر ۱۴۶ ابوداؤد شریف، نمبر ۲۰۵۵) اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ نسب کی وجہ سے جن عورتوں سے نکاح حرام ہے رضاعت کی وجہ سے بھی حرام ہوگا۔ اور تھوڑا سا بھی دودھ ہو اس سے حرمت ثابت ہوگی اس کی دلیل یہ ہے۔ ان عليا وابن مسعود كانا يقولان يحرم من الرضاع قليله وكثيره (نسائی شریف، القدر الذي يحرم الرضاعة ص ۴۵۷ نمبر ۱۳۳۱۳ / دار قطنی ، کتاب الرضاع ج رابع ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۴۳۱۰ رسنن للبیہقی ، باب من قال محرم قلیل الرضاع و کثیر ه ج سابع ص ۷۵۴، نمبر ۱۵۶۴۱) (۲) ان ابن عباس كان يقول ماكان في الحولين وان كانت مصة واحدة فهي تحرم (موطا امام محمد، باب الرضاع ص ۲۷۶) ان آثار سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مرتبہ چوسنے سے بھی حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی (۳) آیت ارضعنکم مطلق ہے۔ کئی گھونٹ کی قید نہیں ہے اس لئے تھوڑ اسا پلانے سے بھی حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ پانچ مرتبہ بچہ دودھ چوسے گا تب حرمت ثابت ہوگی ، اس سے کم سے نہیں۔
[1860] (1) A small amount of breastfeeding or a large amount, if it occurs within the breastfeeding period, prohibition is established. The breastfeeding period according to Imam al-A'zam is two and a half years. If within this period a woman breastfeeds a child even a small amount, then prohibition is established. And marriage to that woman is forbidden for that child. Five gulps are not necessary. (1) The proof of prohibition is the verse that passed: 'and your mothers who nursed you and your sisters from breastfeeding' (Surah al-Nisa 4:23). (2) In a hadith: 'Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, informed him... and he said: Yes, breastfeeding prohibits what birth prohibits.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). From this it is established that those women who are prohibited due to lineage are also prohibited due to breastfeeding. And even a small amount of milk establishes prohibition. Its proof is: 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud used to say: A little or a lot of breastfeeding prohibits.' (Nasa'i, Dar Qutni, Bayhaqi). (2) Ibn Abbas used to say: Whatever is within two years, even if it is one suckle, it prohibits. (Muwatta Imam Muhammad). From these athar it is known that even one suckle establishes prohibition. (3) The verse 'arada'nakum' is absolute; there is no restriction of multiple gulps, therefore even a little feeding establishes prohibition. Imam al-Shafi'i says: The child will suckle five times, then prohibition is established; less than that does not establish it.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on the quantity of breastfeeding required to establish the prohibition of marriage (radīʿa). The Hanafi position: any amount of breast milk, even a single suckle, within the defined breastfeeding period (2.5 years according to Imam Abu Hanifa) creates the same marital prohibitions as lineal blood relations. The author cites the Qur'anic verse 'your mothers who nursed you' and the hadith 'breastfeeding prohibits what birth prohibits' as primary evidence. He further supports with the absolute wording of the verse (no quantity specified) and the sayings of Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Abbas that even one suckle within two years suffices. The Shafi'i position requires five distinct suckles; less does not prohibit. The Hanafi response implicitly argues that the Shafi'i restriction is an addition without evidence, as the Qur'an and hadith did not specify a number. The text then presents the Shafi'i proof: the hadith of Aisha that ten suckles were revealed then abrogated to five, and the Prophet's statement 'one or two suckles do not prohibit.' However, the Hanafi school does not accept this abrogation as established; they rely on the original absoluteness. The passage thus clarifies the Hanafi rule: minimal breastfeeding (qalīl al-riḍāʿ) establishes prohibition.

Key Terms
رضاع (riḍāʿ): Breastfeeding by a woman of a child not her own, establishing a foster relationship that creates marital prohibitions.
حرمت (ḥurmat): The legal prohibition of marriage between individuals due to fosterage, analogized to blood relations.
مدة الرضاع (muddat al-riḍāʿ): The time period within which breastfeeding must occur for the legal effects of fosterage to apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times must a child suckle for the prohibition of marriage to be established?
A) Five times
B) Three times
C) Any amount, even once
D) Ten times

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require any minimum number of suckles; even one suckle within the breastfeeding period establishes the prohibition of marriage.

Duration of Breastfeeding: 30 Months or 2 Years?
Determining the maximum duration for breastfeeding to have legal effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi positions on the breastfeeding period and identify the mufta bihi with its evidence.

Core Idea
Breastfeeding prohibits marriage only if it occurs within the period agreed by the Sahibayn: two years.

This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi disagreement over how long after birth breastfeeding can create a marriage prohibition. We examine Abu Hanifa's cautious 30-month view versus his disciples' strict two-year position, and see why the school favors the latter for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal dispute
The effect of breastfeeding on marriage prohibition depends on timing. Note the two views within Hanafi school and the Shafi'i concurrence with Sahibayn.
The ruling is about the maximum duration, not about other conditions.
2
Analyze the proofs for the two-year view
The Qur'an 2:233 and hadith of Ibn Abbas explicitly mention two years as the complete nursing period.
The hadith 'no breastfeeding except within two years' is particularly explicit.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning for adding six months
He acts out of caution (ihtiyat) to cover the weaning period that may extend beyond two years.
The Muwatta passage shows Abu Hanifa himself acknowledged the original two years but added precaution.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text shows that the Sahibayn's view is relied upon for fatwa, despite Abu Hanifa's personal ihtiyat.
The later school follows the Sahibayn; this is the position of the majority.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a child breastfeeds at 25 months, prohibition is established only if one follows Abu Hanifa; if following mufta bihi, no prohibition.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is clear: marriage between the child and the wet nurse's family depends on which view is taken.

[1861] (2) The breastfeeding period according to Imam Abu Hanifa is thirty months, and according to the two companions (Sahibayn) it is two years. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the original is two years, but he added six months as a precaution so that the period of weaning after two years may be included. So it is clarified in Muwatta Imam Muhammad: 'Abu Hanifa was cautious with six months after the two years, so he said: It prohibits what is within the two years and after them up to six months, that is thirty months; it does not prohibit what is after that. And we do not see that it prohibits, and we see that it does not prohibit what is after two years.' From this statement it is known that for prohibition, two years are the original, and an additional six months are for caution. The Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i say: If a child drinks the milk of a woman within two years, then prohibition is established; if he drinks after that, prohibition is not established. (1) Allah says: 'Mothers shall nurse their children for two complete years for those who desire to complete the nursing' (Qur'an 2:233). This verse indicates two years. (2) Ibn Abbas narrated that the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no breastfeeding except what is within two years.' (Dar Qutni, Bayhaqi). (3) There is also an indication in the hadith of Aisha: 'He said: Look to your sisters; breastfeeding comes only from hunger.'
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage addresses the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute regarding the maximum duration for breastfeeding to produce legal consequences (prohibition of marriage). The key point: Imam Abu Hanifa fixes the period at thirty months (two years plus six months) as a precautionary measure, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, along with Imam al-Shafi'i, hold it to be two years. The author explains that Abu Hanifa's view is based on caution: since the Qur'an (2:233) mentions two years as the complete nursing period, but weaning may extend a few months beyond, he added six months to avoid any doubt. The Muwatta of Imam Muhammad explicitly states this: 'Abu Hanifa was cautious with six months after the two years... we do not see that it prohibits after the two years.' This indicates that the position of the Sahibayn (that no prohibition occurs after two years) is also the more cautious in terms of not extending the prohibition unnecessarily. The proofs for the two-year view include the clear Qur'anic text and the hadith of Ibn Abbas 'no breastfeeding except within two years.' The hadith of Aisha 'breastfeeding comes from hunger' implies that after the child no longer needs milk for sustenance (typically after two years), the ruling changes. Thus, the muftā bihī in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn (2 years) for fatwa, though one may follow Abu Hanifa's ihtiyat in personal practice.

Key Terms
مدة الرضاع (muddat al-riḍāʿ): The time frame within which breastfeeding must occur to establish fosterage prohibition.
صاحبين (ṣāḥibayn): The two major disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
احتیاط (iḥtiyāṭ): A principle of caution in Islamic law, where a scholar adopts a more restrictive view to avoid any possibility of violating the law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position for the breastfeeding period is two years, as supported by the Qur'an and hadith, despite Abu Hanifa's precautionary extension to thirty months.

Duration of Fosterage: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with textual evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the period of fosterage, identify their respective evidences, and explain the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The period of fosterage is two years according to the Sahibayn, and thirty months according to Abu Hanifa based on caution.

Fosterage (rada') creates marriage prohibitions, but only if it occurs within a specific period of the child's life. In this lesson, we explore an important intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa held that the period extends to thirty months, while his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), maintained that it is strictly two years. We will examine the evidence each side uses and understand why the school ultimately adopts the Sahibayn's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
First, note that there are two distinct positions within the Hanafi school on the duration of fosterage that establishes prohibition. State the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn clearly.
Abu Hanifa: 30 months; Sahibayn: 2 years.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's rationale
Read the quote from Muwatta Imam Muhammad. Abu Hanifa agrees that the original period is two years, but he adds six months as a caution (ihtiyat) to ensure that any suckling during the weaning period is not missed. This is a key methodological point.
ihtiyat – legal precaution.
3
Examine the evidence of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn (and Imam al-Shafi'i) rely on Quran 2:233 (two whole years) and the hadith 'La rada'a illa ma kana fi al-hawalayn' (no fosterage except within two years). Also the hadith 'innama al-rada'ah min al-maja'ah' (fosterage is from hunger) indicates it is only for nutritional need, which ends by two years.
These are explicit textual proofs.
4
Determine the practical consequence
The difference matters when a child is breastfed between two and thirty months. According to Abu Hanifa, prohibition is established; according to the Sahibayn, it is not. The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is the Sahibayn's view.
thamarāh al-khilāf – the fruit of the disagreement.

Book of Fosterage. [1861] (2) The period of fosterage according to Abu Hanifa - may Allah have mercy on him - is thirty months, according to them (Sahibayn) it is two years. Its proof is this hadith: from Aisha that she said: 'What was revealed in the Quran was ten known sucklings that make prohibited, then they were abrogated by five known [sucklings], then the Messenger of Allah passed away while it was among what was recited in the Quran.' [1861] (2) The period of fosterage according to Imam Abu Hanifa is thirty months, and according to the Sahibayn is two years. According to Abu Hanifa, the original is two years, but he added six months out of caution so that after two years, while weaning, six months may pass. Thus in Muwatta Imam Muhammad it is clarified: 'Abu Hanifa was cautious with six months after the two years, so he said: it is prohibited what is within the two years and after them up to the completion of six months, that is thirty months; after that it is not prohibited. And we do not see that it is prohibited, and we see that it is not prohibited after the two years.' From this expression it is known that for prohibition, two years are the original, and the extra six months are caution. The Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i say: if one drinks the milk of a woman within two years, prohibition is established; after that, prohibition is not established. (1) In this verse: 'And mothers shall suckle their children for two whole years for those who desire to complete the suckling.' (2:233) This verse says to suckle for two years. (2) From Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no fosterage except what is within the two years.' (3) In this hadith there is also an indication: from Aisha that he said: 'Look at who your sisters are, for fosterage is from hunger.' Footnote: (a) Aisha says: ten sucklings were revealed, then abrogated to five, and the Prophet died while it was recited. (b) He said one or two sucklings do not prohibit. (c) Imam Abu Hanifa was cautious with six months after two years, so he said prohibited within two years and up to six months after, making thirty months; after that not prohibited. (1) Mothers suckle for two years. (e) He said: no fosterage except within two years. (w) He said: look at your sisters (continued on next page). Footnote: (from previous page) who are your sisters; fosterage is from hunger. (a) There is no fosterage except within two years. (b) And fosterage is established from hunger. (c) He said: Yes, fosterage prohibits what lineage prohibits.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the duration of fosterage (rada') that establishes marriage prohibitions. The author first states the core ruling: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the period is thirty months (two years plus six months caution), while according to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is two years. The passage then provides proofs from hadith, including the abrogation of ten sucklings to five, and the hadith 'one or two sucklings do not prohibit.' The author quotes Imam Muhammad's Muwatta to show that Abu Hanifa's position is based on caution (ihtiyat) to ensure no suckling occurs beyond two years without being counted. The Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i rely on the Quranic verse 'two whole years' and the hadith 'no fosterage except within two years' and 'fosterage is from hunger' to limit the period to two years. The practical consequence is that if a child is breastfed between two and thirty months, Abu Hanifa considers it prohibited while the Sahibayn do not. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the Sahibayn: two years, as it is supported by explicit textual evidence.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'ah): Fosterage or suckling that establishes marriage prohibitions.
مدة الرضاع (muddatu al-rada'ah): The legal period during which suckling creates prohibition; disputed between 2 years and 30 months.
حولين (hawlayn): Two years, mentioned in Quran 2:233 as the period for suckling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 1 year
B) 2 years
C) 30 months
D) 6 months

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ultimately holds that fosterage must occur within two years to create prohibition, based on the stronger textual evidence.

beginner

No Prohibition After the Fosterage Period Passes
States the ruling that if the fosterage period has passed, no prohibition is established by suckling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fosterage beyond the prescribed period and apply the hadith proof to determine when prohibition is established.

Core Idea
Fosterage only creates marriage prohibition if it occurs within the nursing period (two years by default).

This lesson addresses a common misunderstanding: does any breastfeeding create a foster relationship? The Hanafi school, based on prophetic hadith, sets a clear time limit. After the prescribed period, even if a child suckles, no marriage prohibition arises. Understanding this boundary prevents unnecessary restrictions in family relations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is suckling after the fosterage period. The ruling: no prohibition (tahrim) is established.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: 'لا رضاع إلا ما كان في الحولين' (no fosterage except within two years) and 'الرضاعة من المجاعة' (fosterage is from hunger).
These are from Darqutni and Bukhari respectively.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negation in the hadith indicates that fosterage is exclusively within the two-year period. The 'hunger' hadith implies that when milk is no longer the primary nourishment (after weaning), suckling does not count.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa extends the period to 30 months, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict it to 2 years. Imam Shafi'i agrees with the Sahibayn.
The text relies on the Sahibayn's view as the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa is: no prohibition after the completion of two years.
This is based on the explicit hadith and is the stronger position in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1862] (3) واذا مضت مدة الرضاع لم يتعلق بالرضاع التحريم اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جس زمانے میں صرف دودھ سے بھوک دور ہو اس زمانے میں دودھ پلانے سے رضاعت ثابت ہوگی۔ یعنی دو سال کے اندر۔ ۱۸۶۲] (۳) اگر رضاعت کی مدت گزر جائے تو دودھ پلانے سے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ مثلا بچے کی عمر دو سال سے زیادہ ہو جائے ۔ اب کسی عورت کا دودھ پیئے تو اس عورت سے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ (۱) او پر حدیث گزرگئی لا رضاع الا ماكان في الحولين (الف) (دار قطنی نمبر ۴۳۱۸) اور دوسری حدیث گزری فانما الرضاعة من المجاعة (ب) ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۵۱۰۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مدت رضاعت ختم ہونے کے بعد بچے کو دودھ پلائے تو اس سے رضاعت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔

In this hadith it is said: in the time when only milk removes hunger, in that time fosterage is established by suckling, i.e., within two years. [1862] (3) If the period of fosterage has passed, then suckling does not establish prohibition. For example, if the child's age exceeds two years, then if he drinks the milk of a woman, prohibition is not established with that woman. (1) The hadith above has passed: 'No fosterage except what is within the two years.' (2) The other hadith passed: 'Fosterage is only from hunger.' From this hadith it is known that after the period of fosterage has ended, if a child is suckled, fosterage is not established.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a straightforward ruling: once the prescribed period of fosterage has ended, suckling does not create marriage prohibitions. The author first gives the Arabic ruling (matn) then explains it in Urdu. The example given is a child over two years old; if such a child breastfeeds, no prohibition arises. The proof is the hadith 'لا رضاع إلا ما كان في الحولين' (no fosterage except within two years) and 'الرضاعة من المجاعة' (fosterage is from hunger), indicating that fosterage only counts when milk is the primary source of nourishment, which is typically within the first two years.

Key Terms
مدة الرضاع (muddatu al-rada'ah): The period during which fosterage counts; after it, no prohibition.
تحريم (tahrim): Prohibition of marriage due to foster relationship.

Fosterage only creates marriage prohibition if it occurs within the first two years of the child's life.

Fosterage Prohibition: General Rule and Two Exceptions
States the general principle that fosterage prohibits what lineage prohibits, with two exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that fosterage prohibits what lineage prohibits and identify the two exceptions where marriage is permissible.

Core Idea
Fosterage mirrors lineage prohibitions except for the mother of a foster sister and the sister of a foster son.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri establishes one of the foundational rules of marriage prohibitions: what is haram by blood is also haram by fosterage. However, the Hanafi school qualifies this rule with two exceptions based on the rationale that foster relationships are narrower than blood ties. Let's examine the general principle and its precise limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule and Its Proof
Read the first part of the passage: 'ويحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب' – 'And from fosterage is prohibited what is prohibited from lineage.' The proof is the hadith: 'نعم الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة.'
The hadith is cited from Bukhari and Muslim.
2
Understand the Analogy
The general principle is an analogy between fosterage and lineage. However, the analogy is not perfect; the text mentions that some relatives who are prohibited by blood are not prohibited by fosterage because they become distant.
3
Learn the First Exception
The mother of a foster sister is ajnabiyya (non-mahram) and thus permissible to marry. In contrast, the mother of a blood sister is one's own mother (mahram) and prohibited.
The passage explains that a foster sister's mother is not a mahram.
4
Learn the Second Exception
The sister of a foster son is permissible to marry because she is ajnabiyya, whereas the sister of a biological son is one's own daughter (mahram) and prohibited.
The passage emphasizes the distinction based on the nature of the relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1863] (۴) ويحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب ر یہاں سے فرمانا چاہتے ہیں کہ جو لوگ نسب سے حرام ہوتے ہیں وہی لوگ رضاعت سے بھی حرام ہوتے ہیں۔ لیکن کچھ لوگ ایسے بھی ہیں جو نسب سے تو حرام ہو جائیں گے لیکن رضاعت کی وجہ سے وہ دور کے رشتہ دار ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اس لئے وہ لوگ حرام نہیں ہوں گے ۔ اس کی تفصیل آگے آرہی ہے۔ رضاعت سے حرمت کی دلیل گزر گئی۔ فقال : نعم الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة (ج) ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۵۰۹۹، مسلم شریف ۱۴۴۴) [1864 (۵) الا ام اخته من الرضاع فانه يجوز ان يتزوجها ولا يجوز ان يتزوج ام اخته من النسب رضاعی بہن کی ماں اجتنبیہ ہوگی اس لئے اس سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور نسبی بہن کی ماں تو خود کی ماں بن گئی اس لئے اس سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ یا اپنی سوتیلی بہن کی ماں سوتیلی ماں ہوگی اور باپ کی مدخول بھا ہوگی اس لئے اس سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ [1865) (۶) اور رضاعی بیٹے کی بہن سے جائز ہے نکاح کرنا۔ اور نہیں جائز ہے نبی بیٹے کی بہن سے شادی کرنا۔ رضاعی بیٹے کی بہن اجتنبیہ ہوگی۔ اس لئے اس سے نکاح جائز ہوگا۔ اور اپنے نسبی بیٹے کی بہن اپنی بیٹی ہوگی اس لئے اس سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
[1863] (4) And from fosterage is prohibited what is prohibited from lineage. From here he intends to say: those who are prohibited by lineage, the same are prohibited by fosterage. But there are some who would be prohibited by lineage but due to fosterage they become distant relatives, so they are not prohibited. The detail will come later. The proof for prohibition by fosterage has passed: 'Yes, fosterage prohibits what birth prohibits.' [1864] (5) Except: the mother of a foster sister, for it is permitted to marry her, and it is not permitted to marry the mother of a lineage sister. The mother of a foster sister is a non-mahram (ajnabiyya), so marrying her is permissible. The mother of a lineage sister is one's own mother, so marrying her is impermissible. Or the mother of one's stepsister is a stepmother and is the father's consummated wife, so marrying her is impermissible. [1865] (6) And from marriage is permitted the sister of a foster son, and it is not permitted to marry the sister of a lineage son. The sister of a foster son is a non-mahram, so marrying her is allowed. The sister of one's own lineage son is one's own daughter, so marrying her is not allowed.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage states the general principle that fosterage establishes the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage, supported by the hadith 'الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة'. Then it lists two exceptions: (1) The mother of one's foster sister is permissible to marry, whereas the mother of a blood sister is one's own mother (or stepmother if half-sister) and thus prohibited. (2) The sister of one's foster son is permissible to marry, whereas the sister of one's blood son is one's own daughter and thus prohibited. The rationale is that foster relationships do not extend to all relatives like blood; only the specific individuals mentioned in hadith are prohibited. The exceptions prevent an overly broad application of the analogy.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Blood lineage or kinship
رضاع (rada'ah): Foster relationship through suckling

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, because of foster relationship
C) Only if the foster sister is from two years

Key Takeaway
Fosterage prohibits what lineage prohibits, with specific exceptions: the mother of a foster sister and the sister of a foster son are permissible to marry.

Time Limit for Fosterage Prohibition
Ruling that fosterage only creates prohibition within two years

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time limit for fosterage and apply the hadith proofs to determine whether prohibition is established.

Core Idea
Fosterage only creates prohibition if suckling occurs within the first two years of life.

Fosterage (rida') establishes mahram relationships, but only if the suckling happens within a specific window. The Hanafi school strictly limits this to the first two years based on clear prophetic hadith. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the legal effect of suckling after two years: does it create prohibition?
The ruling is negative: no prohibition.
2
Locate the proof
Find the hadith cited and note their sources.
Hadith: 'لا رضاع إلا ما كان في الحولين' and 'فانما الرضاعة من المجاعة'.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith texts prove the ruling.
The negation 'لا رضاع' and the condition 'ما كان في الحولين' show that only suckling within the two-year period counts.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify that the Shafi'i school differs and understand their basis.
Shafi'i considers the period flexible up to weaning; Hanafi insists on strict two-year limit.
5
Apply to a scenario
Test yourself: a child of 2 years and 1 day drinks from a woman. Does she become mahram?
No, because the time limit has passed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا مضت مدة الرضاع لم يتعلق بالرضاع التحريم [بخاری شریف، باب من قال لارضاع بعد حولین ص ۶۴ نے نمبر ۵۱۰۲ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی رضاعة الكبيرص ۲۸۸ نمبر ۲۰۵۸] اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جس زمانے میں صرف دودھ سے بھوک دور ہو اس زمانے میں دودھ پلانے سے رضاعت ثابت ہوگی۔ یعنی دو سال کے اندر۔ [۱۸۶۲] (۳) اگر رضاعت کی مدت گزر جائے تو دودھ پلانے سے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ مثلا بچے کی عمر دو سال سے زیادہ ہو جائے ۔ اب کسی عورت کا دودھ پیئے تو اس عورت سے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ (۱) او پر حدیث گزرگئی لا رضاع الا ماكان في الحولين (الف) (دار قطنی نمبر ۴۳۱۸) اور دوسری حدیث گزری فانما الرضاعة من المجاعة (ب) ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۵۱۰۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مدت رضاعت ختم ہونے کے بعد بچے کو دودھ پلائے تو اس سے رضاعت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔
When the period of suckling has passed, prohibition does not attach to suckling. [Bukhari, Bab man qala la rada'a ba'da hawlayn, p.64 no.5102; Abu Dawud, Bab fi rada'ati al-kabir, p.288 no.2058] This hadith states that at the time when hunger is only satisfied by milk, suckling establishes fosterage. That is, within two years. [1862] (3) If the suckling period passes, then suckling does not establish prohibition. For example, if the child's age exceeds two years and then he drinks a woman's milk, prohibition is not established with that woman. (1) A hadith has passed: 'There is no fosterage except what is within the two years' (al-Daraqutni no.4318) and another hadith 'Indeed fosterage is from hunger' (Bukhari no.5102). From this hadith it is known that after the suckling period ends, if a child is fed milk, fosterage is not established.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that suckling after the two-year period does not create marital prohibitions. The author provides proof from hadith: the Prophet ﷺ said 'There is no fosterage except what is within the two years' and 'Fosterage is from hunger.' The wisdom is that after two years, milk is no longer the primary nutrition for the child. Thus, if a child over two years drinks a woman's milk, she does not become a mahram. This is the Hanafi position, based on these ahadith.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): The act of a woman suckling a child, thereby creating a legal foster relationship.
حولين (hawlayn): Two years, the period within which fosterage is effective according to the Hanafi school.

General Rule: Fosterage Prohibits Like Lineage
Statement of the principle that fosterage creates same prohibitions as blood lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding fosterage prohibitions and identify which relatives are included and excluded.

Core Idea
Fosterage forbids what birth forbids, but not for distant relatives.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle in Hanafi nikah: fosterage creates mahram relationships just like blood lineage. The author cites the famous hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to establish this. However, there are important exceptions that prevent the analogy from applying to distant relatives. Understanding this rule helps you determine whom one may marry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal principle
Read the first sentence: 'ويحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب'. This is the core rule: fosterage prohibits the same as lineage.
2
Locate the dalil
The author references the hadith 'نعم الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة'. Recognize this as a mutawatir hadith (Bukhari, Muslim).
This hadith is accepted by all schools.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'تحرم' is a prohibition verb; 'ما تحرم الولادة' indicates that the prohibitions of birth are the standard. The hadith equates fosterage to birth in establishing mahram relations.
The analogy is clear but not absolute; exceptions exist.
4
Note the exceptions
The passage immediately adds that some blood relatives become 'distant relatives' through fosterage and thus are not prohibited. This is a key Hanafi distinctive.
Details of exceptions are given later in the text.
5
Apply the principle
Given a scenario, decide if a marriage is prohibited. Use the hadith as proof and remember the exception for distant relatives.
Example: foster mother and foster sister are prohibited; foster maternal aunt is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب [۱۸۶۳] (۴) اور دودھ پلانے سے حرام ہوتے ہیں وہ لوگ جو نسب سے حرام ہوتے ہیں۔ ر یہاں سے فرمانا چاہتے ہیں کہ جو لوگ نسب سے حرام ہوتے ہیں وہی لوگ رضاعت سے بھی حرام ہوتے ہیں۔ لیکن کچھ لوگ ایسے بھی ہیں جو نسب سے تو حرام ہو جائیں گے لیکن رضاعت کی وجہ سے وہ دور کے رشتہ دار ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اس لئے وہ لوگ حرام نہیں ہوں گے ۔ اس کی تفصیل آگے آرہی ہے۔ رضاعت سے حرمت کی دلیل گزر گئی۔ فقال : نعم الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة (ج) ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۵۰۹۹، مسلم شریف ۱۴۴۴)
And what is forbidden due to lineage is forbidden due to fosterage. [1863] (4) From suckling, those people become forbidden who are forbidden due to lineage. Here it is meant that the people who are forbidden due to lineage, the same people are also forbidden due to fosterage. But there are some people who become forbidden due to lineage but due to fosterage they become distant relatives, so they are not forbidden. Details will come later. The proof for prohibition from fosterage has already passed: He (the Prophet) said: 'Yes, fosterage forbids what birth forbids' (Bukhari no.5099, Muslim 1444).
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage states the general rule that fosterage creates the same marital prohibitions as those of blood lineage (nasab). The author mentions that there are exceptions: some relations that are mahram by blood are not mahram by fosterage due to distant relationship (e.g., the mother of a foster-sister). The proof is from the hadith 'الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة' – fosterage forbids what birth forbids.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Blood lineage or kinship by birth.
ولادة (wiladah): Childbirth or birth, referring to blood relations.
رضاع (radha'): Fosterage or suckling relationship that establishes mahramiyyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة' establishes the principle, but the Hanafi school applies it with exceptions for distant relatives.

The Mother of a Foster-Sister: A Permissible Marriage Exception
Exception to the rule on fosterage mahram relations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the mother of a foster-sister and explain why she is not a mahram.

Core Idea
A man may marry his foster-sister's mother because she is a non-mahram (ajnabiyya).

The Hanafi school holds that fosterage creates mahram relationships similar to lineage for the child and the foster family, but not all extensions. This passage clarifies an exception: the mother of a foster-sister is not a mahram, so marriage is permissible. We will explore the reasoning and distinguish between lineage and fosterage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Marrying the mother of one's foster-sister. What is the ruling? It is permissible (ja'iz).
This is an exception to the general rule that fosterage prohibits like lineage.
2
Distinguish between lineage and fosterage
Contrast with the mother of a blood sister (mahram) and the mother of a half-sister (step-mother, also mahram). Understand why the foster-sister's mother is different.
The mother of a blood sister is one's own mother; the mother of a half-sister is a step-mother.
3
Recognize the reasoning (ajnabiyya vs mahram)
The mother of a foster-sister is not related by blood or fosterage to the man; she is an unrelated woman (ajnabiyya). Therefore, marriage is permissible.
Fosterage does not create a mahram relationship between the foster child and the foster-sister's mother.
4
Consider cross-madhhab difference
Some schools may argue that the mother of a foster-sister becomes mahram by extension. Note the Hanafi response: the prohibition is limited to specific relatives.
This ikhtilaf is valid; both positions are based on different interpretations of the scope of fosterage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الا ام اخته من الرضاع فانه يجوز ان يتزوجها ولا يجوز ان يتزوج ام اخته من النسب [۱۸۶۴ (۵) مگر رضاعی بہن کی ماں کہ جائز ہے اس سے نکاح کرنا۔ اور نہیں جائز ہے کہ نبی بہن کی ماں سے شادی کرے۔ رضاعی بہن کی ماں اجتنبیہ ہوگی اس لئے اس سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور نسبی بہن کی ماں تو خود کی ماں بن گئی اس لئے اس سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ یا اپنی سوتیلی بہن کی ماں سوتیلی ماں ہوگی اور باپ کی مدخول بھا ہوگی اس لئے اس سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
Except the mother of his sister from fosterage, for it is permissible for him to marry her, and it is not permissible for him to marry the mother of his sister from lineage. [1864] (5) But the mother of a foster-sister, it is permissible to marry her. And it is not permissible to marry the mother of a blood sister. The mother of a foster-sister is a non-mahram (ajnabiyya), so it is permissible to marry her. And the mother of a blood sister became his own mother, so marriage with her is not permissible. Or the mother of his half-sister is his step-mother and is the father's wife (who has been consummated), so marriage with her is not permissible.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage gives an exception to the general rule. A man cannot marry his blood sister's mother because she is his own mother. However, his foster-sister's mother is not related to him by blood or fosterage; she is an ajnabiyya (unrelated woman), so marriage with her is permissible. The author distinguishes between full-blood sister's mother (i.e., his mother) and half-sister's mother (his step-mother), both of whom are mahram.

Key Terms
رضاعية (rada'iyya): Foster-relative, a person related through suckling.
اجنبية (ajnabiyya): A woman who is not a mahram; unrelated, permissible to marry.
محرم (mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, fosterage, or marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible for a man to marry the mother of his foster-sister?
A) Yes, because she is not a mahram
B) No, because she is like his mother
C) Yes, but only if the foster-sister is from his mother's milk
D) No, because she is related by fosterage

Key Takeaway
A man may marry his foster-sister's mother because she is not within the prohibited degrees of fosterage; she remains an unrelated woman (ajnabiyya).

Sister of Foster-Son: Permissible to Marry
Exception: sister of foster-son is permissible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the sister of a foster-son and explain why she is not mahram.

Core Idea
A foster-son's sister is not mahram; only direct foster relationships create prohibition.

We have learned that a foster-son is mahram to his foster-mother, but what about his sisters? Many assume the prohibition extends to all the foster-child's relatives. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: the sister of a foster-son is ajnabiyya (non-mahram), and marriage to her is permissible. The proof lies in the distinction between foster and blood lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the text: 'the sister of his son from fosterage: it is permissible for him to marry her.' State the ruling: marriage is permissible (ja'iz).
2
Locate the Proof
The author contrasts with the blood son's sister, who is one's own daughter and therefore mahram. The proof is an analogy (qiyas) of difference: fosterage does not create extended family ties.
The underlying principle is that only the foster relationship itself (mother-son) creates mahramiyyah, not the foster-child's siblings.
3
Understand the Rationale
Explain why the sister of a blood son is mahram: she is the man's own daughter. For a foster-son, his sister is unrelated to the foster-father; she is ajnabiyyah.
This is a direct application of the rule: 'al-walad li'l-firash' does not apply to fosterage.
4
Note Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider the sister of a foster-son as mahram by extension. Recognize this as legitimate ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi view is mufta bihi in our school.
5
Apply to Similar Cases
If a man has multiple foster-children, can he marry the sister of one of them? Yes, because each foster-child's sister is ajnabiyya, unless she is also his foster-daughter.
The prohibition only arises if the woman herself is the foster-daughter (i.e., she was suckled by the man's wife).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واخت ابنه من الرضاع [ص۸۱] يجوز ان يتزوجها ولا يجوز ان يتزوج اخت ابنه من النسب [ص۸۲] [۱۸۶۵) (۶) اور رضاعی بیٹے کی بہن سے جائز ہے نکاح کرنا۔ اور نہیں جائز ہے نبی بیٹے کی بہن سے شادی کرنا۔ رضاعی بیٹے کی بہن اجتنبیہ ہوگی۔ اس لئے اس سے نکاح جائز ہوگا۔ اور اپنے نسبی بیٹے کی بہن اپنی بیٹی ہوگی اس لئے اس سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
And the sister of his son from fosterage: it is permissible for him to marry her, and it is not permissible for him to marry the sister of his son from lineage. [1865) (6) And from the sister of a foster-son, marriage is permissible. And it is not permissible to marry the sister of a blood son. The sister of a foster-son is ajnabiyya (non-mahram), so marriage with her is permissible. And the sister of one's own blood son is one's own daughter, so marriage with her is not permissible.

Commentary
This is another exception. A man's blood son's sister is his daughter, who is mahram. But his foster-son's sister is not related to him; she is ajnabiyya, so marriage is permissible. The author emphasizes that the prohibition is only through direct foster relationship, not through extended family.

Key Terms
ابن الرضاع (ibn al-rada'): Foster-son, a boy who was suckled by a woman and thereby becomes her foster-son.
أجنبية (ajnabiyya): A woman who is not a mahram; marriage to her is permissible.

D) No, due to the foster relationship

Key Takeaway

Prohibition of Marrying Foster-Son's Wife
Ruling with proof from Quran and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the wife of a foster-son, cite the Quranic verse (4:23) and the athar from Iyas ibn 'Amir, and explain the qiyas that extends the prohibition to foster-sons.

Core Idea
Marrying the wife of a foster-son is as forbidden as marrying the wife of a biological son — fosterage creates the same permanent prohibition.

Marriage prohibitions due to fosterage (rida'ah) are a nuanced area of Hanafi fiqh. This lesson focuses on a specific ruling: a man cannot marry the wife of his foster-son. The clear prohibition in the Quran for biological sons is extended by qiyas to foster-sons, supported by a prophetic athar. Understanding this ruling requires grasping how Hanafi usul treats the qualifying phrase 'from your loins' and how analogy operates in establishing mahram relationships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a man marrying the wife of his foster-son. The Hanafi ruling is that this is haram (permanently forbidden).
The ruling applies regardless of whether the foster-son was breastfed by the man's current wife or a former wife.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The primary evidence is from the Quran: 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins' (an-Nisa 4:23). This verse explicitly prohibits marrying the wife of a biological son.
The athar from Iyas ibn 'Amir explicitly includes foster-son's wife in the prohibition.
3
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation of the verse
Hanafi usul treats the phrase 'from your loins (min aslabikum)' as a description (sifah) rather than a condition (shart). Therefore, the prohibition is not limited to biological sons; it extends to any son-like relationship, such as foster-son, via qiyas.
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider 'min aslabikum' a restrictive condition, so they do not extend the prohibition.
4
Apply the qiyas
The effective cause (illah) is the son-like relationship created by fosterage. Since a foster-son is treated like a biological son in other prohibitions (e.g., marriage to the foster-mother), the same applies to his wife.
The qiyas is based on the principle that 'fosterage renders prohibited what lineage renders prohibited' (al-rada' yuharrimu ma yuharrimu min al-nasab).
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that the wife of a foster-son is not mahram, because the Quranic phrase limits the prohibition to biological sons. For them, a man may marry his foster-son's wife.
The practical consequence: Hanafi muftis will rule it haram; Shafi'i muftis may allow it under certain conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is not permissible for him to marry the wife of his son from fosterage, just as it is not permissible for him to marry the wife of his son from lineage. [1866] (7) And it is not permissible to marry the wife of one's foster-son, just as it is not permissible to marry the wife of one's blood son. This woman suckled a child, so that child becomes the foster-son of her husband. Now, marrying that woman (the wife of the foster-son) is forbidden, because she becomes his foster-daughter-in-law. Just as if it were his own blood son, marrying his wife would be forbidden. The Quranic verse says: 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins' (Surah an-Nisa 4:23). This verse makes it forbidden to marry the wife of one's own biological son. The wife of an adopted son is excluded; one can marry her. But the wife of a foster-son is included, so marriage with her is forbidden. (2) There is an athar: 'My paternal uncle Iyas ibn 'Amir said: He (the Prophet) said: Do not marry the woman whom your father's wife suckled, nor the wife of your son (by fosterage), nor the wife of your brother (by fosterage).' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab tahrimu min ar-rada' ma hurrima min al-waladat wa inna laban al-fahl muharram, juz' 7 p.746 no.15616). This athar states that do not marry the wife of a foster-son.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage rules that a man cannot marry the wife of his foster-son. The evidence includes the Quranic verse about 'wives of your sons from your loins', which is interpreted to include foster-sons because the foster-son is like a biological son in terms of prohibition. The athar from Iyas ibn 'Amir explicitly prohibits marrying the wife of a foster-son. The Hanafi position is that this prohibition is permanent.

Key Terms
امرأة ابنه (imra'at ibnihi): The wife of one's son, whether biological or foster.

Key Takeaway
The wife of a foster-son is permanently prohibited for marriage by analogy to the prohibition for biological sons, based on the Hanafi interpretation of Quran 4:23 and a prophetic athar.

Laban al-Fahl: The Milk of the Man Creates Fosterage Prohibitions
Ruling with proof: establishing laban al-fahl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on laban al-fahl and identify which relatives of the husband become mahram to the suckled child.

Core Idea
The husband's milk establishes full fosterage kinship through his line.

This lesson explores the Hanafi concept of laban al-fahl – the milk attributed to the man who caused the lactation. A widespread misunderstanding is that only the nursing woman becomes a mahram, but the Hanafi school firmly holds that the husband and his close male relatives also become permanently forbidden to the suckled child. We will unpack the ruling, its practical example, and the decisive evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that laban al-fahl 'attaches prohibition' (يتعلق به التحريم). This means the suckled girl becomes haram for the husband (the fahl), his father, his sons, and his grandfather. Recognize that this goes beyond the nursing woman alone.
The prohibition is permanent (haram), exactly like lineage-based mahram.
2
Understand the causal link
The milk is attributed to the husband because it came down due to his intercourse with the nursing woman. The husband is the 'owner of the milk' (sahib al-laban). This causal link is the basis for extending prohibitions to his relatives.
If milk comes without intercourse (e.g., artificial means), the husband does not become a mahram in the Hanafi school.
3
Work through the concrete example
The text gives the example of Fatima (the wet nurse), her husband Zaid, and the suckled girl Sajida. Sajida becomes haram for Zaid, Zaid's father becomes her foster-grandfather, and Zaid's biological son Khalid becomes her foster-brother. Trace each relationship.
The same logic applies if the suckling child is a boy – the husband becomes his foster-father, his daughters become foster-sisters, etc.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith of Aisha (ra) is cited. The Prophet ﷺ called the man her 'uncle' (عم) despite only the woman having suckled her. This proves that the fosterage relationship extends through the husband's lineage. Identify the key phrase: 'He is your uncle' (فانه عمک).
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning (thubut qati) and its dalala is clear (qati) – it decisively establishes laban al-fahl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولبن الفحل يتعلق به التحريم وهو ان ترضع المرأة صبية فتحرم هذه الصبية على زوجها [ ۱۸۶۷ (۸) مرد کے دودھ سے حرمت متعلق ہوتی ہے وہ یہ کہ عورت دودھ پلائے بچی کو تو حرام ہو جائے یہ بچی اس کے شوہر پر اور شوہر کے باپ پر اور شوہر کے بیٹوں پر اور وہ شوہر جس سے عورت کا دودھ اترا ہے وہ دودھ پینے والی بچی کا باپ ہوگا۔ مثلا فاطمہ نے ساجدہ بچی کو دودھ پلایا تو فاطمہ کا شوہر مثلا زید ہے جس کی وطی سے فاطمہ کو دودھ اترا ہے۔اس شوہر کے لئے ساجدہ دودھ پینے والی بچی حرام ہوگئی۔ اسی طرح شوہر زید کا باپ بچی کیلئے دادا بن گیا۔ اس لئے زید کا باپ ساجدہ سے شادی نہیں کرسکتا۔ زید کانسبی بیٹا خالد ساجدہ بچی کا رضاعی بھائی بن گیا اس لئے ساجدہ اس رضاعی بھائی سے شادی نہیں کر سکتی۔ صحبت کرنے کی وجہ سے دودھ اترا ہے اس لئے شوہر کا اصول یعنی باپ دادا اور فروع یعنی بیٹا اور پوتا بچی پر حرام ہو گئے۔ جیسے نبی باپ، دادا اور بھائی حرام ہو جاتے ہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشہ قالت جاء عمى من الرضاعة يستأذن على فابيت ان آذن له حتى استأمر رسول الله الا الله فقال رسول الله الا الله فلج علیک فانه عمک، قالت انما ارضعتنى المرأة ولم يرضعني الرجل قال فانه عمک فلیلج علیک (ب) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی لبن الفحل ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۱۴۸ر بخاری شریف باب لبن المحل ص ۷۶۴ نمبر ۵۱۰۳ر مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم الرضاعة من ماء المحل ص ۴۶۶ نمبر ۱۴۴۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ رضاعی باپ کا جو
And the milk of the man (laban al-fahl) – prohibition is attached to it, and that is that a woman suckles a girl, then this girl becomes forbidden for her husband. [1867] (8) The milk of the man establishes prohibition. That is, when a woman suckles a baby girl, then this girl becomes forbidden for her husband, and for the husband's father, and for the husband's sons. And that husband, due to whose intercourse the woman's milk came down, becomes the father of the suckling girl. For example, Fatima suckled a girl named Sajida; Fatima's husband is Zaid, due to whose intercourse Fatima's milk came down. For this husband, Sajida (the suckling girl) becomes forbidden. Similarly, Zaid's father becomes the grandfather of the girl, so Zaid's father cannot marry Sajida. Zaid's biological son Khalid becomes the foster-brother of Sajida, so Sajida cannot marry this foster-brother. Because the milk came down due to intercourse, therefore the husband's ascendants (father, grandfather) and descendants (son, grandson) become forbidden to the girl, just as (in lineage) father, grandfather, and brother become forbidden. (2) There is a hadith from Aisha: She said: My uncle from fosterage came and sought permission to enter, but I refused permission until I consulted the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). The Messenger of Allah said: 'He may enter upon you, for he is your uncle.' She said: 'Only the woman suckled me, not the man.' He said: 'He is your uncle, so let him enter upon you.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi laban al-fahl, p.218 no.1148; Bukhari, Bab laban al-fahl, p.764 no.5103; Muslim, Bab tahrim ar-rada'a min ma' al-fahl, p.466 no.1445). This hadith states that the foster-father's (i.e., the husband's) ...
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage explains the concept of laban al-fahl – the milk of the man (meaning the milk that results from a woman being impregnated by a man). If a woman suckles a girl, that girl becomes mahram to her husband (the 'owner' of the milk) and to his ascendants and descendants. For example, the husband becomes her foster-father, his father becomes her foster-grandfather, and his son becomes her foster-brother. The evidence is from the well-known hadith of Aisha, where the Prophet ﷺ confirmed that her foster-uncle (brother of her foster-father) is indeed her uncle and may enter upon her. This proves that the foster relationship extends through the husband's line as well.

Key Terms
لبن الفحل (laban al-fahl): Literally 'milk of the man', meaning the milk that is produced by a woman due to a specific man's intercourse, thereby making that man the 'father' of the suckling child for purposes of fosterage.
فحل (fahl): Male, specifically the man whose intercourse caused the milk to come down.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the woman who suckled her
B) The woman's husband, his father, and his sons
C) Only the woman's biological relatives
D) No one besides the woman

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the milk of the man (laban al-fahl) creates permanent fosterage prohibitions for the husband and his male ascendants and descendants, supported by the hadith of Aisha.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
6 min
Marrying the Wife of a Foster Son is Prohibited
States ruling with Quran and Hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the wife of a foster son and cite the Quranic and hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Marrying the wife of a foster son is as forbidden as marrying the wife of a biological son.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in the Hanafi school: the prohibition of marrying the wife of one's foster son. The Quran explicitly prohibits marrying the wife of one's biological son, but what about a son through fosterage? The Hanafi school establishes that fosterage creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood relations, and this passage provides both textual and analogical proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marrying the wife of one's foster son. The ruling is explicit: 'la yajuz' – it is not permissible. This is a prohibition (haram).
The text analogizes directly to the biological son's wife.
2
Locate the primary dalil: Quran 4:23
The verse says: 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins.' The Hafiz interprets that 'your sons' includes foster sons because fosterage creates a similar relationship. The qualifier 'from your loins' excludes adopted sons, not foster sons.
The Quranic text is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalala on this inclusion.
3
Examine the secondary dalil: athar from Iyas ibn Amir
The athar explicitly states: 'Do not marry the wife of your son.' The commentary clarifies that this includes the foster son’s wife, as the prohibition extends to the wife of one's foster brother and father's foster son.
This athar is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and is used as supporting evidence.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
The Hanafi position relies on the principle that fosterage (rada') renders unlawful what is unlawful by birth. The Quranic word 'ibnaikum' is taken in its general sense, covering both biological and foster sons, because the cause of prohibition (relationship through the husband's milk) is analogous.
The analogy is based on the shared 'illa of relationship through milk.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may restrict the prohibition to biological sons only, arguing that the Quranic qualifier 'min aslabikum' limits the meaning. However, the Hanafi school includes foster sons via analogy and the athar.
The practical effect (thamarah) is that in the Hanafi school, a man cannot marry the wife of his foster son, while in other schools it may be permissible.

Source Text

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثالث كتاب الرضاع يجوز ان يتزوجها ولا يجوز ان يتزوج اخت ابنه من النسب [ ۱۸۶۶ (۷) ولا يجوز ان يتزوج امرأة ابنه من الرضاع كما لا يجوز ان يتزوج امرأة ابنه من النسب [ ۱۸۶۶ (۷) اور نہیں جائز ہے کہ شادی کرے اپنی رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی سے جیسا کہ نہیں جائز ہے کہ شادی کرے اپنے بیٹے کی بیوی سے۔ ی بیوی نے کسی کے بچے کو دودھ پلایا تو وہ بچہ اس شوہر کا رضاعی بیٹا بن گیا، اب اس کی بیوی سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ رضاعی بہو بن گئی۔ جس طرح اپنا نسبی بیٹا ہوتا تو اس کی بیوی سے نکاح حرام ہوتا۔ آیت میں ہے۔ وحلائل ابنائكم الذين من اصلابکم ( آیت ۲۳ سورۃ النسا ۴ ) اس آیت میں اپنے صلبی بیٹے کی بیوی سے نکاح کرنا حرام قرار دیا۔ اس سے متنبنی بیٹے کی بیوی نکل گئی۔ اس سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی داخل ہے اور اس سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ حدثنی عمی ایاس بن عامر قال قال لا تنكح من ارضعته امرأة ابيك ولا امرأة ابنك ولا امرأة اخيك (الف) (سن للمبتی ، باب تحرم من الرضاع ما حرم من الولادة وان لبن المحل محرم ج سابع ہیں ۷۴۶، نمبر ۱۵۶۱۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی سے شادی مت کرو۔ حاشیہ : (الف) ایاس بن عامر نے فرمایا جس کو دودھ پلایا ہے وہ باپ کی بیوی سے شادی نہ کرے، اور نہ رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی سے، اور نہ رضاعی بھائی کی بیوی سے۔
The explanation al-Thamiri, volume 3. Book of Fosterage. It is permissible to marry her, but it is not permissible to marry the sister of his son from lineage. [1866] (7) And it is not permissible to marry the wife of his son from fosterage, just as it is not permissible to marry the wife of his son from lineage. [1866] (7) Urdu: And it is not permissible to marry the wife of his foster son, just as it is not permissible to marry the wife of his own son. This wife breastfed someone's child, so that child becomes the foster son of the husband; now marrying his wife is forbidden, because she became his foster daughter-in-law. Similarly, if it were his own son, marrying his wife would be forbidden. The verse says: 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins' (Surah al-Nisa 4:23). This verse prohibits marrying the wife of one's own biological son. The wife of an adopted son is excluded; one may marry her. But the wife of a foster son is included, and marrying her is forbidden. (2) There is an athar: 'My uncle Iyas ibn Amir narrated to me, he said: He said: Do not marry the one whom the wife of your father has breastfed, nor the wife of your son, nor the wife of your brother.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: Fosterage makes unlawful what birth makes unlawful, and the milk of the stallion is unlawful, volume 7, p. 746, no. 15616) This athar states: Do not marry the wife of your foster son. Footnote (a): Iyas ibn Amir said: The one who has been breastfed should not marry the wife of his father, nor the wife of his foster son, nor the wife of his foster brother.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm with dalil). It states the prohibition of marrying the wife of one's foster son, analogizing to the prohibition of marrying the wife of one's biological son based on Quran 4:23. The commentary explains that when a woman breastfeeds a child, that child becomes a foster son to her husband, making the child's wife (the woman who breastfed) forbidden to the husband as a foster daughter-in-law. The verse specifically mentions 'sons from your loins,' which excludes adopted sons but includes foster sons because fosterage creates a similar relationship. The athar from Iyas ibn Amir reinforces this ruling, explicitly prohibiting marriage to the wife of one's foster son. The footnote clarifies that the prohibition also extends to the wife of one's father's foster son and the wife of one's foster brother, indicating that all such relationships are treated like blood relations in terms of marriage prohibitions.

Key Terms
الرضاع (al-rada'): Fosterage: the relationship established when a woman breastfeeds a child, making the child a mahram to certain relatives.
خَتَنٌ/صِهْر (khatn/sihr): In-law relationship; here specifically the wife of one's son (biological or foster).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, is it permissible to marry the wife of one's foster son?
A) Yes, because fosterage does not create in-law relationships.
B) No, it is forbidden just like the wife of a biological son.
C) It is permissible if the foster son is not from the husband's loins.
D) It is makruh but not haram.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, marrying the wife of a foster son is haram, just like marrying the wife of a biological son, based on Quran and hadith.

Laban al-Fahl: The Milk of the Stallion Establishes Prohibition
Ruling and evidence for prohibition based on foster father's milk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on laban al-fahl and apply it to identify which relatives become mahram through fosterage.

Core Idea
The husband’s milk extends prohibition to his ascendants and descendants, just as blood relations do.

This lesson examines the principle of laban al-fahl, which determines that the husband whose wife breastfeeds a child becomes the foster father, making his entire lineage mahram to that child. The ruling is based on the hadith of Aisha and the athar of Ibn Abbas, as explained in the Urdu commentary.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Principle
Define laban al-fahl: the milk attributed to the husband (stallion) because it results from his intercourse. This milk creates foster relationships tied to him.
The husband is the source of prohibition, not just the breastfeeding woman.
2
Identify the Affected Parties
List who becomes mahram: the husband (foster father), his father (foster grandfather), his sons (foster brothers), and his brothers (foster uncles) as per the hadith.
The text gives the example: Fatima breastfeeding Sajida makes Sajida forbidden to Zaid, his father, and his son Khalid.
3
Connect to the Hadith Evidence
Analyze the hadith of Aisha: the Prophet declared her foster uncle (the foster father’s brother) as her mahram, proving that the husband’s male relatives are included.
‘He is your uncle’ – the word ‘uncle’ establishes mahramiyyah.
4
Apply to the Athar of Ibn Abbas
Two children breastfed by different wives of the same husband cannot marry because they share the same foster father (the husband). This confirms that prohibition is based on the husband.
‘The insemination is one’ – the husband is the common factor.
5
Distinguish from Blood Relations
Note that the prohibitions mirror those of blood lineage (father, grandfather, brother, uncle) but only through the husband’s side, not the wife’s.
The breastfeeding woman’s own brother does not become mahram to the child.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

دادا اور بھائی حرام ہو جاتے ہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشہ قالت جاء عمى من الرضاعة يستأذن على فابيت ان آذن له حتى استأمر رسول الله الا الله فقال رسول الله الا الله فلج علیک فانه عمک، قالت انما ارضعتنى المرأة ولم يرضعني الرجل قال فانه عمک فلیلج علیک (ب) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی لبن الفحل ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۱۴۸ر بخاری شریف باب لبن المحل ص ۷۶۴ نمبر ۵۱۰۳ر مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم الرضاعة من ماء المحل ص ۴۶۶ نمبر ۱۴۴۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ رضاعی باپ کا جو بھائی تھا جس کو رضاعی چا کہتے ہیں۔ اس سے پردہ نہیں ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ بھی محرم بن گئے۔ اور رضاعی باپ کے اصول اور فروع بھی محرم بن گئے۔ ان سے بھی چچا ہیں۔ حضرت عائشہ نے فرمایا مجھے عورت نے دودھ پلایا ہے مرد نے نہیں۔ آپ نے فرمایا وہ آپ کے رضاعی چچا ہیں آپ کے پاس آ سکتے ہیں۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابن عباس سے پو چھا گیا کہ ایک آدمی کو دوباندیاں ہیں۔ ان میں سے ایک نے ایک لڑکی کو دودھ پلایا اور دوسری نے لڑکے کو تو کیا لڑکی کے لئے حلال ہے کہ لڑکے سے شادی کرے؟ حضرت نے فرمایا نہیں۔ حمل ایک ہی آدمی کا ہے۔
The milk of the stallion is that by which prohibition is established. It is that a woman breastfeeds a girl, then this girl becomes forbidden to her husband. [1867] (8) Urdu: The husband's milk establishes prohibition. It is that a woman breastfeeds a girl, then this girl becomes forbidden to her husband, and to the husband's father, and to the husband's sons. And that husband from whom the woman's milk came will be the father of the breastfed girl. For example, Fatima breastfed the baby Sajida, then Fatima's husband, say Zaid, from whose intercourse Fatima's milk came. For this husband, the breastfed baby Sajida becomes forbidden. Similarly, the husband Zaid's father becomes the grandfather of the girl, so Zaid's father cannot marry Sajida. Zaid's biological son Khalid becomes the foster brother of Sajida, so Sajida cannot marry this foster brother. Because the milk came due to intercourse, therefore the husband's ascendants (father, grandfather) and descendants (son, grandson) become forbidden to the girl, just as the biological father, grandfather, and brother become forbidden. (2) Hadith: 'Aisha said: My foster uncle came and asked permission to enter, but I refused until I consulted the Messenger of Allah. He said: Let him enter, for he is your uncle. She said: Only the woman breastfed me, not the man. He said: He is your uncle, so let him enter.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on the milk of the stallion, p. 218, no. 1148; Bukhari, chapter on the milk of the stallion, p. 764, no. 5103; Muslim, chapter on prohibition of fosterage from the water of the stallion, p. 466, no. 1445) This hadith shows that the brother of the foster father, called the foster uncle, is not required to observe hijab. This indicates that he also becomes a mahram. And the ascendants and descendants of the foster father also become mahram; marrying them becomes forbidden. (2) From Ibn Abbas: He was asked about a man who has two slave girls; one of them breastfed a girl and the other breastfed a boy. Is it permissible for the boy to marry the girl? He said: No, the insemination is one. (Tirmidhi, chapter on the milk of the stallion, p. 218, no. 1149; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: Fosterage makes unlawful what birth makes unlawful, and the milk of the stallion is unlawful, vol. 7, p. 453) This athar: A master had two slave girls; both were milked. One slave girl breastfed a boy and the other breastfed a girl. Since both have the same foster father, they cannot marry each other. This shows that the husband from whose intercourse the milk came is considered in establishing prohibition. Footnote (b): Aisha says: My foster uncle came and asked permission to enter. I refused until I consulted the Prophet. He said: He may come to you because he is your uncle. Aisha said: Only the woman breastfed me, not the man. He said: He is your uncle, so let him enter. Footnote (a): Ibn Abbas was asked: A man has two slave girls; one breastfed a girl and the other breastfed a boy. Is it permissible for the girl to marry the boy? He said: No, the insemination is one.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the principle of 'laban al-fahl' (milk of the stallion). It states that the husband whose wife breastfeeds a child becomes the foster father, and his relatives (ascendants and descendants) become mahram to that child. The text provides a detailed example: Fatima breastfeeds Sajida; then Sajida becomes forbidden to Fatima's husband Zaid (her foster father), to Zaid's father (her foster grandfather), and to Zaid's son Khalid (her foster brother). This is because the milk originates from intercourse with the husband. The hadith of Aisha demonstrates that the foster father's brother is also a mahram, as the Prophet allowed her foster uncle to enter. The athar of Ibn Abbas shows that even if two different women breastfeed a boy and a girl, if the husband (the source of milk) is the same, the children are considered foster siblings and cannot marry. The key point is that prohibition revolves around the husband (the stallion), not just the breastfeeding woman.

Key Terms
لبن الفحل (laban al-fahl): The milk of the stallion: prohibition established through the husband whose wife breastfeeds a child.
الرضاعة (al-rada'ah): Fosterage; the act of breastfeeding that establishes legal relationships.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
