A) Only the breastfeeding woman's husband.
B) The husband, his father, and his sons.
C) Only the husband's sons, not his father.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
The milk of the stallion (laban al-fahl) makes the husband's entire lineage mahram to the breastfed child, establishing prohibitions equivalent to blood relations.

Marrying the Sister of a Foster Brother is Permissible
Ruling with examples on foster marriage permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on marrying the sister of a foster brother and explain why she is considered a stranger (ajnabiyya).

Core Idea
A foster brother's sister is not your foster sister — she is a stranger, so marriage is permissible.

A common confusion arises when two men share a foster mother: are all relatives of one foster brother also mahram to the other? This passage clarifies that only the direct foster relationship creates kinship; the biological sister of a foster brother remains a non-mahram, making marriage to her permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is marrying the sister of one's foster brother. The ruling is permissible (mubah).
The passage explicitly states 'it is permissible' (يجوز).
2
Understand the basis for permissibility
The sister of the foster brother is not a foster relative to the man because she was not breastfed by his foster mother. She remains a stranger (ajnabiyya).
Foster relationships are established only through direct breastfeeding.
3
Distinguish from the foster sibling themselves
If the man and the sister had been breastfed by the same woman, they would be foster siblings and marriage would be forbidden. But here the sister is the biological sibling of the foster brother, not a foster sister.
The example in the passage: Zaid and Khalid are foster brothers; Khalid's own sister is permissible for Zaid.
4
Apply the same logic to half-siblings
Similarly, a paternal half-brother may marry a maternal half-sister because they share only one parent and are not mahram to each other.
The diagram illustrates Abdur Rashid (paternal half-brother) marrying Aisha (maternal half-sister of Abdur Rahim).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۶۸](۹) ويجوز ان يتزوج الرجل باخت اخيه من الرضاع كما يجوز ان يتزوج باخت اخيه من النسب [ ۱۸۶۸ (۹) اور جائز ہے کہ آدمی رضاعی بھائی کی بہن سے شامی کرے جیسا جائز ہے کہ نبی بھائی کی بہن سے شادی کرے۔ اس کی مثال اس طرح ہے کہ جیسے باپ شریک بھائی اس کی ماں شریک بہن ہو۔ جائز ہے اس کے باپ شریک بھائی کے لئے یہ کہ شادی کرے اس کی ماں شریک بہن سے۔ یہاں دو مسکے ہیں۔ پہلا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ رضاعی بھائی کی اپنی بہن سے شادی کرنا جائز ہے۔ مثلا زید کا رضاعی بھائی خالد تھا۔ ان دونوں نے ایک تیسری عورت سے دودھ پیا تھا۔ اب خالد کی اپنی بہن تھی جو زید کے لئے راجیہ تھی اس لئے زید کے لئے جائز ہے کہ خالد کی اپنی بہن سے شادی کرلے۔ اس لئے کہ خالد کی بہن زید کے لئے اجنبیہ ہے۔ البتہ زید یا خالد اگر لڑکی ہو تو ان دونوں کے درمیان شادی نہیں ہو سکتی۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں رضاعی بھائی بہن ہیں۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سوتیلے بھائی کی ماں شریک بہن سے نکاح جائز ہے۔ اس نقشہ کو دیکھیں۔ شوهر زید ماں رضیہ باپ خالد ماں سعیدہ XAN بھائی عبدالرشید بہن عائشہ بھائی عبد الرحیم عبدالرشید کی شادی عبدالرحیم کی ماں شریک بہن عائشہ سے جائز ہے
[1868] (9) And it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster brother, just as it is permissible to marry the sister of his brother from lineage. [1868] (9) Urdu: And it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster brother, just as it is permissible to marry the sister of his biological brother. Its example is like a paternal half-brother and maternal half-sister. It is permissible for the paternal half-brother to marry the maternal half-sister. There are two issues here. First: It is permissible for a man to marry the own sister of his foster brother. For example, Zaid's foster brother was Khalid; both drank milk from a third woman. Now Khalid had his own sister, who was a stranger for Zaid. So it is permissible for Zaid to marry Khalid's own sister, because Khalid's sister is a non-mahram for Zaid. However, if Zaid or Khalid are girls, then marriage between them is not allowed because they are foster brother and sister. Second issue: It is permissible to marry the maternal half-sister of a half-brother. See this diagram: Husband Zaid, mother Radhiyya, father Khalid, mother Sa'ida, ... brother Abdur Rashid, sister Aisha, brother Abdur Rahim. Abdur Rashid marrying Abdur Rahim's maternal half-sister Aisha is permissible.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that permits a man to marry the sister of his foster brother. The author explains that just as one can marry the sister of a biological brother, one can marry the sister of a foster brother because there is no foster relationship between the man and that sister. Two examples are given: first, if two men share a foster mother, they are foster brothers; each may marry the other's biological sister because she is a stranger to him. Second, regarding half-siblings: a paternal half-brother may marry a maternal half-sister because they share only one parent. The diagram illustrates that Abdur Rashid (paternal half-brother) can marry Aisha (maternal half-sister of Abdur Rahim).

Key Terms
أخ من الرضاع (akh min al-rada'): Foster brother: a male who was breastfed by the same woman as another.
أجنبية (ajnabiyya): A woman who is not a mahram; permissible to marry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Zaid and Khalid are foster brothers (both breastfed by the same woman). Is it permissible for Zaid to marry Khalid's biological sister?
A) Yes, because she is not a mahram to Zaid.
B) No, because she is considered Zaid's foster sister.
C) It is makruh.
D) Only if Khalid agrees.

Key Takeaway
The sister of a foster brother is a stranger; marriage to her is permissible.

Foster-Father Becomes Mahram: Hanafi Ruling and Dalil
Ruling on foster-father's mahram status with Ibn Abbas evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the foster-father and his ascendants/descendants become mahram to the nursing woman, and cite the hadith of Ibn Abbas as evidence.

Core Idea
The foster-father is as mahram as the birth father—marriage with him and his lineage is permanently haram.

In this passage, the matn establishes a key ruling on fosterage (rida'): not only the wet nurse but also her husband (the foster-father) becomes a mahram to the nursing woman, and so do his fathers and sons. The commentator explains why this makes marriage haram with the entire adoptive paternal line. The ruling is then supported by a powerful hadith from Ibn Abbas, which uses the principle 'the male is one' to block marriage between a boy and girl nursed by different women under the same master. Understanding this foundation is essential to grasp the Hanafi position on fosterage.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify who becomes mahram according to the matn: the foster-father, his fathers, and his sons.
The matn says 'وعلى آبائه وابنائه ويصير الزوج... ابا للمرضعة'.
2
Extract the legal principle
The husband whose milk provision triggers the nursing becomes a father to the nursed infant; his lineage is treated like blood lineage.
This is based on the principle 'al-liqahu wahid' from the hadith.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the Ibn Abbas narration: two slave girls of the same master nurse a boy and a girl. The master is the common 'father' — marriage is forbidden.
Reference: Tirmidhi and Bayhaqi.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'la' shows prohibition, and 'al-liqahu wahid' (the male is one) shows the cause: shared paternity through milk renders the children milk-siblings.
Dalala is qati even though thubut is zanni.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is only extend mahram to the wet nurse and her husband, not to the husband's lineage. The Hanafi school extends to all ascendants/descendants of the foster-father.
This difference has practical implications in marriage contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى آبائه وابنائه ويصير الزوج الذى نزل لها منه اللبن ابا للمرضعة [بھائی؟] تھا جس کو رضاعی باپ کہتے ہیں۔ اس سے پردہ نہیں ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ بھی محرم بن گئے۔ اور رضاعی باپ کے اصول اور فروع بھی محرم بن گئے۔ ان سے بھی شادی کرنا حرام ہو گیا (۲) عن ابن عباس انه سئل عن رجل له جاريتان ارضعت احداهما جارية والاخرى غلاما ايحل للغلام ان يتزوج الجارية ؟ فقال: لا، اللقاح واحد (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في لبن المحل ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۱۴۹رسن للبیہقی ، باب تحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من الولادة وان لين الحل يحرم ج سابع ص۴۵۳) اس اثر میں ایک آقا کی دو باندیاں تھیں۔ اور دونوں کو دودھ ابتر تا تھا۔ ایک باندی نے لڑکے کو دودھ پلایا اور دوسری نے لڑکی کو دودھ پلایا تو چونکہ دونوں کا رضاعی باپ ایک ہے اس لئے یہ دونوں آپس میں شادی نہیں کر سکتے ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس شوہر کی محبت سے دودھ اترا ہے حرمت میں اس کا اعتبار ہے۔
And upon his fathers and his sons, and the husband from whom the milk came becomes a father to the nursing woman. [He] was [the one] called foster-father. There is no veiling from him. From this it is known that he also becomes a mahram. And the foster-father's ascendants and descendants also become mahram. Marrying them becomes forbidden. (2) From Ibn Abbas that he was asked about a man who has two slave girls; one of them nursed a girl and the other nursed a boy. Is it permissible for the boy to marry the girl? He said: No, the male (father) is one. (Reference: Tirmidhi, etc.) In this narration, there was a master with two slave girls, and both were producing milk. One slave girl nursed a boy and the other nursed a girl. Since both have one foster-father, these two cannot marry each other. From this it is known that the husband from whose love the milk comes, his consideration is in prohibition.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn establishing that the foster-father (the husband whose milk caused the nursing) becomes a father to the nursing woman, and his fathers and sons are also mahram. The commentator explains that the foster-father is a mahram, so hijab is not required, and his lineage (ascendants and descendants) also become mahram, making marriage with them haram. A supporting hadith from Ibn Abbas is cited: a man had two slave girls, one nursed a boy and the other a girl. Since the milk came from the same master (the husband), the boy and girl cannot marry. This demonstrates that the husband who is the source of the milk determines the prohibition, not merely the wet nurse. The ruling is a foundation for fosterage relationships in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
رضاع (riḍāʿ): Fosterage or suckling; the act of a woman nursing a child who is not her own, creating legal prohibition of marriage.
محرم (maḥram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, fosterage, or marriage ties.

Marrying the Sister of a Foster-Brother: Scope of Foster Prohibition
Ruling and analogy on foster-brother's sister

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the sister of a foster-brother is ajnabiyyah and apply the Hanafi qiyas from blood relations to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
Foster-sibling prohibition is limited to direct foster-siblings; marrying a foster-sibling's sibling is permissible.

This lesson addresses a common point of confusion: does the prohibition of marrying a foster-sibling extend to their biological siblings? The Hanafi ruling, based on clear analogy with blood relations, confirms it does not. By examining the text, you will understand the precise scope of foster relationships in marriage law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the key phrase: 'ويجوز ان يتزوج الرجل باخت اخيه من الرضاع' (it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster-brother). Note the ruling is jā'iz (permissible).
The verb 'يجوز' indicates permission, not obligation.
2
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The text says 'كما يجوز ان يتزوج باخت اخيه من النسب' (just as it is permissible to marry the sister of his blood brother). This is a qiyas jali: the asl (blood brother) shares the same 'illa—the woman is not a mahram. The far' (foster brother) is analogous because his sister is also not a mahram.
The 'illa is that she is not a direct foster or blood sister to the man.
3
Apply the analogy to an example
The commentary gives an example: a paternal half-brother (same father) can marry the maternal half-sister (same mother) of his half-brother, because they are only half-siblings, not full. Similarly, in the story of Radiya, Aisha (daughter from first husband) is ajnabiyyah to Abdurrashid (son from second husband by another wife).
This illustrates that only direct foster-siblings are mahram; their siblings remain ajnabi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۶۸](۹) ويجوز ان يتزوج الرجل باخت اخيه من الرضاع كما يجوز ان يتزوج باخت اخيه من النسب اور جائز ہے کہ آدمی رضاعی بھائی کی بہن سے شادی کرے جیسا جائز ہے کہ نبی بھائی کی بہن سے شادی کرے۔ اس کی مثال اس طرح ہے کہ جیسے باپ شریک بھائی اس کی ماں شریک بہن ہو۔ جائز ہے اس کے باپ شریک بھائی کے لئے یہ کہ شادی کرے اس کی ماں شریک بہن سے۔ النسب وذلك مثل الاخ من الاب اذا كان له اخت من امه جاز لاخيه من ابيه ان يتزوجها رضیہ نے پہلی شادی زید سے کی تھی اس سے عائشہ پیدا ہوئی۔ پھر دوسری شادی خالد سے کی اس سے عبدالرحیم پیدا ہوا۔ جس کی بنا پر عائشہ رحیم کی ماں شریک بہن ہوئی۔ ادھر خالد نے ایک اور شادی سعیدہ سے کی جس سے عبدالرشید پیدا ہوا جو عبدالرحیم کا سوتیلا بھائی ہوا۔ اس لئے عبدالرشید کی شادی عائشہ سے ہو سکتی ہے۔ کیونکہ عائشہ عبدالرشید کے لئے اجنبیہ ہے۔
(9) And it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster-brother, just as it is permissible to marry the sister of his blood brother. And it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster-brother, just as it is permissible to marry the sister of a blood brother. An example: like a paternal half-brother, if he has a maternal half-sister, it is permissible for his paternal half-brother to marry her. And (the commentary continues): That is like a brother from father: if he has a sister from mother, it is permissible for his brother from father to marry her. Radiya first married Zaid and gave birth to Aisha. Then she married Khalid and gave birth to Abdurrahim. So Aisha became Abdurrahim's maternal half-sister. Meanwhile, Khalid married Sa'idah and gave birth to Abdurrashid, who became Abdurrahim's step-brother. Therefore, Abdurrashid's marriage to Aisha is permissible, because Aisha is a non-mahram for Abdurrashid.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This lesson states the ruling that it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster-brother. The justification is analogy with blood relations: just as one can marry the sister of a blood brother, one can marry the sister of a foster-brother. The commentator elaborates with an example: a paternal half-brother (same father) can marry the maternal half-sister (same mother) of his half-brother, because they are not blood-siblings. Similarly, in the story: Radiya had children from two marriages. Her daughter Aisha is the maternal half-sister of Abdurrahim. Abdurrashid is Abdurrahim's paternal half-brother (same father). Since Aisha is not a mahram to Abdurrashid (they share no foster or blood relation), marriage is halal. This distinguishes between direct foster siblings (who cannot marry) and siblings of foster siblings (who can).

Key Terms
رضاعی بھائی (riḍāʿī bha'ī): Foster-brother; a male who suckled from the same woman as oneself.
اجنبی (ajnabī): A person not related in a prohibited degree; marriage is permissible with them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The sister of a foster-brother is not a mahram; marriage to her is permissible, as confirmed by qiyas on blood relations.

Two Infants on One Breast: Foster-Sibling Prohibition
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that any two infants nursed from the same breast become foster-siblings and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Two infants sharing one breast become foster-siblings; marriage between them is permanently haram.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on fosterage (radaa'). The passage states that if two infants are nursed from the same breast—regardless of time—they become mahram (unmarriageable) to each other. The commentator supports this with authentic hadith, including the case of the Prophet and Hamza, and the testimony of a black woman. Understanding this ruling is essential for determining marriage prohibitions arising from milk-relationship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm level?
Act: marriage between two individuals who were nursed from the same breast. Ruling: haram.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadith proofs cited by the commentator.
Hadith of the Prophet and Hamza (Bukhari) and hadith of the black woman (Bukhari).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do the hadith prove the ruling? What specific words or actions indicate the prohibition?
The Prophet's explicit prohibition of marrying Hamza's daughter because she is his foster-niece shows that foster-siblings are mahram.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement among schools on this ruling?
Shafi'is require multiple nursing sessions; Hanafi holds one session sufficient.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is mufta bihi and why?
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view; the hadith are explicit and general.

Source Text

[۱۸۶۹](۱۰) وكل صبيين اجتمعا على ثدى واحد لم يجز لاحدهما ان يتزوج الآخر [ ١٧٠ ا ا ولا يجوز ان يتزوج المرضعة احدا من وُلد التي ارضعت. يه پہلے ہی مسئلے کا اعادہ ہے۔ یعنی ماں نے بچی کو بھی دودھ پلایا اور بچے کو بھی دودھ پلایا تو بچی کا نکاح اس بچے سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں رضاعی بھائی بہن ہوئے۔ حديث میں ہے کہ حضور اور حضرت حمزہ نے حضرت ثوبیہ سے دودھ پیا تھا جس کی وجہ سے دونوں رضاعی بھائی ہو گئے تھے۔ اور حضرت حمزہ کی بیٹی رضاعی بھتیجی ہوگئی تھی۔ اور آپ نے فرمایا تھا کہ حضرت حمزہ کی بیٹی میرے اوپر پیش نہ کرو وہ رضاعی بھتیجی ہے۔ (بخاری شریف) (۳) ایک آدمی نے ایک عورت سے شادی کی تو ایک عورت نے گواہی دی کہ میں نے تم دونوں کو دودھ پلایا ہے۔ اس لئے تمہاری شادی اس عورت سے حلال نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک ہی چھاتی سے دونوں نے دودھ پیا ہے۔ (بخاری) انت مری : پستان۔ [۱۸۷۰] (۱۱) اور نہیں جائز ہے کہ شادی کرے دودھ پینے والی بچی کسی ایسے بچے سے جس کو اس کی ماں نے دودھ پلایا ہے۔ یہ پہلے ہی مسئلے کا اعادہ ہے۔
(10) And any two infants who are brought together on one breast, it is not permissible for one of them to marry the other. And it is not permissible for the nursing woman to marry any of the children of the woman who nursed. This is a repetition of the previous issue, meaning the mother nursed both a girl and a boy, so the girl's marriage to that boy is not permissible because they are foster-siblings. In a hadith, the Prophet and Hamza both nursed from Thuwaybah, so they became foster-brothers. And Hamza's daughter became a foster-niece. And the Prophet said: Do not present Hamza's daughter to me, for she is my foster-niece. (Bukhari) (3) A man married a woman, then a black woman came and testified that she had nursed both of them, so the marriage is not permissible because they both suckled from one breast. (Bukhari) (11) And it is not permissible for the nursing girl to marry any boy whom her mother nursed. This is a repetition of the earlier issue.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This lesson combines two rulings from the matn. The first (10) states that any two infants who suckle from the same breast, regardless of time, become foster-siblings and cannot marry. The commentator supports this with the hadith of the Prophet and Hamza, who were both nursed by Thuwaybah, making them foster-brothers, and the Prophet forbade marrying Hamza's daughter. Another hadith about a man whose marriage was invalidated because a woman testified she had nursed both him and his wife. The second ruling (11) is a repetition: a girl nursed by a woman cannot marry a boy also nursed by that woman, as they are foster-siblings. The commentator notes this is the same rule.

Key Terms
ثدى (thady): Breast; the physical source of milk. Two infants sharing the same breast establishes fosterage.
رضاع (radaa'): Fosterage through breastfeeding, creating mahram relationships.

Prohibition of Marrying Sister of Foster Father
Ruling with brief explanation and principle reference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of marrying the sister of the foster father and explain the underlying principle of rada'.

Core Idea
A foster child cannot marry the sister of his foster father because rada' creates the same prohibitions as blood lineage.

This lesson presents a clear ruling from the chapter on rada' (fosterage). It establishes that the sister of the husband of the nursing woman becomes a foster paternal aunt, making marriage with her permanently prohibited. The ruling is based on the well-known hadith principle that breast-milk prohibits what birth prohibits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited relationship
The foster child (the boy who was breastfed) is prohibited from marrying the sister of the husband of the nursing woman. This sister becomes his foster paternal aunt.
2
Recognize the rationale
The husband of the nursing woman is considered the foster father. Therefore, his sister is equivalent to a paternal aunt in the foster relationship.
3
Recall the general principle
The hadith 'الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة' (Breast-milk prohibits what birth prohibits) establishes that rada' creates the same marital prohibitions as blood lineage.
4
Apply the principle to the case
Since a real paternal aunt is mahram (permanently prohibited for marriage), the foster paternal aunt is also mahram by rada'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱ (۱۲) ولا يتزوج الصبي المرضع اخت زوج المرضعة لانها عمته من الرضاع [۱۸۷۱) (۱۲) اور نہیں جائز ہے دودھ پینے والے بچے کا نکاح دودھ پلانے والی عورت کے شوہر کی بہن سے اس لئے کہ وہ رضاعی پھوپی ہے۔ دودھ پلانے والی ماں کا شوہر رضاعی باپ ہوا اور اس کی بہن رضاعی پھوپی ہوئی ہے اس لئے دودھ پینے والے بچے کا نکاح رضاعی پھوپی سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ پہلے گزر چکا ہے الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة (بخاری شریف نمبر ۵۰۹۹) کہ نسب سے جس طرح حرام ہوتا ہے رضاعت سے بھی حرام ہوتا ہے۔
And a foster child boy may not marry the sister of the husband of the nursing woman, because she is his paternal aunt by rada'.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: a boy who has been breastfed by a woman cannot marry the sister of that woman's husband. The reason given is that the husband becomes the foster father, so his sister becomes the foster paternal aunt. This is based on the established principle that breast-milk creates the same prohibitions as blood lineage (حديث: الرضاعة تحرم ما تحرم الولادة). The ruling is straightforward and does not involve a proof beyond this principle.

Key Terms
عمته من الرضاع (ammatuhu min al-rada'): His paternal aunt through fosterage; the sister of the foster father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Milk Mixed with Food: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn on Rad'
Intra-madhhab dispute on tahrim when milk is mixed with food

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa rules that mixing breast milk with food negates fosterage prohibition and distinguish the Sahibayn's counter-position.

Core Idea
Milk must independently satisfy hunger to create prohibition; mixing with food strips its legal effect.

The Hanafi school holds that fosterage (rada') prohibits marriage when a child nurses on breast milk that alleviates hunger. But what if the milk is mixed with food? Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ on whether the prohibition survives the mixture. This lesson unpacks their reasoning through the hadith 'al-rada'atu min al-maja'ah'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Mixed Milk
Abu Hanifa states: if milk is mixed with food, no fosterage prohibition attaches, even if milk is the predominant ingredient. The Sahibayn dissent, holding that prohibition does attach due to the milk's predominance.
The term 'ghalib' (predominant) is key to the Sahibayn's argument.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's Proof
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith: 'O Aisha, consider your brothers; indeed, fosterage is from hunger.' He interprets 'min al-maja'ah' (from hunger) to mean that the milk itself must be the sole source alleviating hunger. When mixed with food, the food becomes the primary substance and satisfies hunger, not the milk.
The hadith is narrated by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Contrast the Sahibayn's Reasoning
The Sahibayn argue that since milk is predominant in the mixture, it remains the effective cause ('illa) of prohibition. They give greater weight to quantitative predominance over the qualitative condition of independence.
This is a classic example of competing legal considerations: text (nass) vs. predominant element (ghalabah).
4
Recognize the Practical Consequence
If a child is fed a porridge cooked with breast milk, Abu Hanifa says no rada' is established, so the child may marry the wet nurse's family. The Sahibayn say rada' is established, creating marriage restrictions. This 'thamarah al-khilaf' illustrates the real impact of the dispute.
The tarjih (preferred view) is not specified here but Abu Hanifa's view is textually stronger.

(۱۴) واذا اختلط بالطعام لم يتعلق بها ، التحريم وان كان اللبن غالبا عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا رحمهما الله تعالى يتعلق به ، التحريم اگر دودھ کھانے کے ساتھ مل جائے تو اس کے ساتھ حرمت متعلق نہیں ہوگی اگر چہ غالب ہوا امام ابو حنیفیہ کے نزدیک۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں اس کے ساتھ حرمت متعلق ہوگی۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی نظر حدیث کا لفظ يا عائشة انظرن من اخوانكن فانما الرضاعة من المجاعة (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشهادة على الانساب والرضاع المستفيض والموت القديم ص ۳۶۰ نمبر ۲۶۴۷ر مسلم شریف، باب انما ارضاعة من المجاعة ص ۴۶۹ نمبر ۱۴۵۵) میں الرضاعة من المجاعة کی طرف گئی ہے۔ اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صرف دودھ سے بھوک ختم ہو تو اس دودھ سے رضاعت ثابت ہوگی۔ اور دودھ کو کھانے میں ملا دیا تو کھانا اصل ہو گیا اس سے بھوک دور ہوگی۔ اور دودھ تابع ہو گیا اب اس سے بھوک دور ہونا اصل نہیں رہا۔ اس لئے اس سے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ کانہ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ دودھ غالب ہے اس لئے دودھ اصل ہے۔ اس لئے حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ حاشیه : (الف) اے عائشہ ! بھائیوں کو دیکھنا، رضاعت تو بھوک دور کرنے سے ہوتی ہے۔
And if it is mixed with food, prohibition does not attach even if the milk is predominant according to Abu Hanifa; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say prohibition attaches.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding milk mixed with solid food (e.g., cooked). Abu Hanifa rules that even if milk predominates, no fosterage prohibition arises because the mixture becomes a food where food is the primary substance. He relies on the hadith 'الرضاعة من المجاعة' (fosterage is from hunger), indicating that only when milk alone satisfies hunger does it create prohibition. When mixed with food, hunger is satisfied by the food, not the milk. The two companions (Sahibayn) argue that because milk is predominant in quantity, it remains the effective cause, so prohibition attaches. The footnote provides a translation of the hadith: 'O Aisha, consider your brothers; indeed, fosterage is from hunger.'

Key Terms
الرضاعة من المجاعة (al-rada'atu min al-maja'ah): Fosterage is from hunger: only milk that alleviates hunger on its own creates prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does mixing milk with food nullify the prohibition of fosterage?
A) Because food is a solid and milk is a liquid.
B) Because the milk becomes subsidiary to the food in satisfying hunger.
C) Because the hadith prohibits rada' from mixtures.
D) Because the Sahibayn disagree.

Key Takeaway
Mixing milk with food nullifies its legal effect for fosterage according to Abu Hanifa because the food, not the milk, becomes the primary source of nourishment.
